<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pharmacology">Pharmacology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pharmacology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Samuel Wamamba</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="branches-of-pharmacology">Branches of pharmacology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#branches-of-pharmacology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p><strong>Pharacotherapeutic</strong>: (clinical pharmacology)
It deals with relative effect of drugs in the human system for various disorders or it deals with the effect of a drug that the Dr. orders for treating a human patient
—The study of drug action in man‖.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Pharmacodynamic</strong>:
Which deal with experimental (science pertaining to theories of drug action or it deals with the interactions between chemical components of living system and foreign chemical including drugs that enter living organism.
—What the drug does to the body‖</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Pharmacokinetics</strong>:
Which is the study of drug’s alteration during its way through the body or it's the study of the fate of drug in the body as it is absorbed, distributed, bound to or localized in tissues, biotransformed and excreted.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-science-concerns-itself-with">The science concerns itself with:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-science-concerns-itself-with" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Drug absorption and distribution.</li>
<li>Drug plasma concentration.</li>
<li>Therapeutic plasma levels.</li>
<li>Concentration of the active drug at the target site.</li>
<li>Rate of metabolism.</li>
<li>Rate of excretion.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="these-parameters-in-turn-affected-by">These parameters in turn affected by:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#these-parameters-in-turn-affected-by" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Physiochological nature of the drug e.g. lipid solubility.</li>
<li>Formulation of the drug.</li>
<li>Route of administration.</li>
<li>Binding of the drug to plasma and/or tissue (bioavailability)</li>
<li>Individual characteristics of the patient.</li>
<li>Concomitant diseases.</li>
<li>Concomitant administration of food or other drugs.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sources-of-drugs">Sources of drugs:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources-of-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Drugs and biologic products are derived from 4 main sources:</p>
<ol>
<li>Plants: examples of which are digitalis.</li>
<li>Animals and human: from which drugs such as insulin, epinephrine are obtained.</li>
</ol>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Minerals or mineral products: examples such as iodine and iron.</li>
<li>Chemicals: made in laboratories. They are pure drugs and some of them are simple such as sodium bicarbonate where others are complex synthesis such as sulfonomides and adrenocorticosteroids.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Active constituents of plant drugs:</strong>
The leaves, roots, seeds and other parts of plants may be dried or otherwise processed for use as medicine and they are known as crude drugs.</p>
<p>On separation of these active constituents, the resulting pure form are:</p>
<ol>
<li>More potent.</li>
<li>Usually produce effects more reliable than those of the crude drugs.</li>
<li>More poisonous and the dose must be smaller.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Common Drug Preparations:</strong></p>
<p><strong>1. Solutions and Suspensions:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Aqueous Solutions: have one or more substance dissolved in water e.g. Epinephrine nasal sol.</li>
<li>Aqueous suspensions: are preparations of finally divided drugs either intended for suspension or already in suspension in some suitable liquid vehicle.</li>
<li>Sterile suspensions are intended for intramuscular or subcutaneous injections but they can't be given intravenously or intrathecally into spinal fluid.</li>
<li>Oral suspensions are NOT sterile and must NOT be injected.</li>
</ul>
<p>N.B.: - Suspensions tend to settle slowly and should be CHAKED WELL before use to provide uniform distribution of the drug.</p>
<ul>
<li>Elixir: clear fluid containing water and alcohol designed for oral use, usually has a sweetener added.</li>
<li>Syrup: medication dissolved in a concentrated sugar solution.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>2. Dosage Forms:-</strong>
Capsules, controlled- release or sustained- release capsules, tablets, pills and troches are used to provide a drug or mixture of drugs into definite doses and avoid the inconvenience of preparing the dose from dry powder.</p>
<ul>
<li>Capsules and coated tablets are a convenient way of giving drugs that have unpleasant taste.</li>
<li>Capsules:- are solid dosage form for oral use medication in a powder, liquid or oil form are incased in gelatin shell, capsule colored to avoid</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>mistakes in product identification.</p>
<p><strong>Tablet</strong>: Powered dosage form compressed into hard disks or cylinders. In addition to primary drug, they contain binders (adhesive to allow powder to stick together) and disintegrates (to promote tablet dissolution).</p>
<p><strong>NOTES</strong></p>
<p>1- Some gelatin capsules and tablets may be coated with substances that resist the action of gastric juice so that will not disintegrate until they reach the alkaline secretions of the intestine.
2- Sustained – release dosage forms contain small particles of the drug coated with materials that require a varying amount of time to dissolve. This provides for a long continuous period of absorption and effect.</p>
<p><strong>Pill</strong>: Solid dosage form containing one or more drug. Recently, they were replaced by tablets.</p>
<p><strong>Ampoules and vials</strong>: Ampoules and vials contain powder or liquid drug usually intended for injection.</p>
<p><strong>Disposable Syringes</strong>: Disposable syringes containing single dose of drug preparations are widely used.</p>
<p><strong>Large volume intravenous Solutions</strong>: In glass, flexible plastic or semi-rigid plastic usually of 250, 500, 100 ml e.g. 0.9% sodium chloride.</p>
<p><strong>Intermittent IV. Solution</strong>: These solutions are similar to the I.V. solutions except they come in smaller volumes.</p>
<p><strong>3-Additional Formulations</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Drops</strong>: are aqueous solutions that anesthetize, soothe or medicate eyes, ears, or nose.</li>
<li><strong>Installations</strong>: are aqueous solution instilled into the body cavities or wound and allowed to dwell there in contact with tissue.</li>
<li><strong>Foams and aerosols</strong>: are powders or solutions for spraying skin as topical anesthesia to soothe or protect or inhalation for bronchodilation.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>4- Others</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Lotions</strong>: Liquid suspensions or dispersions used for external applications e.g. calamine lotion.</li>
<li><strong>Creams</strong>: aqueous and oily emulsions to soothe skin.</li>
<li><strong>Ointments</strong>: semisolid preparations of medical substances in some type of base such as petrolatum lanolin used for their soothing or bacteriostatic effect. <strong>Ophthalmic ointment</strong>: Are sterile (e.g. Synthomycin) ophthalmic ointment.</li>
<li><strong>Pasts</strong>: Ointment- like preparations suited for only external</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>application. e.g. Zinc oxide past.</p>
<p>6</p>
<ul>
<li>Suppositories: are mixtures of drugs with a firm base that can be molded in shapes suitable for insertion manually or with an applicator into body cavity or orifice e.g. Aminophylline supp.
N.B.: they should be kept cool.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="drug-absorption-distribution-metabolism-and-excretion">Drug Absorption, Distribution metabolism and Excretion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-absorption-distribution-metabolism-and-excretion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Absorption: Is the process that involves the movement of drug molecules from the site of entry into the body to the circulating fluid.</li>
<li>The process begins at the site of administration and is essential (to the subsequent processes, distribution, metabolism and excretion).</li>
<li>Absorption as a process varies according to the route of administration, dosage form and the dose of the drug.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factors-affecting-drug-absorption">Factors Affecting Drug Absorption:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-affecting-drug-absorption" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-nature-of-the-absorbing-surface-cell-membrane-through-which-the-drug-must-traverse">1- Nature of the absorbing surface (cell membrane), through which the drug must traverse.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-nature-of-the-absorbing-surface-cell-membrane-through-which-the-drug-must-traverse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>The drug molecule may pass through a single layer of cells (intestinal epithelium) faster than several layers of cells (skin).</li>
<li>Size of the absorbing surface.</li>
</ul>
<p>N.B.: The more extensive the absorbing surface, the greater the absorption and more rapid effect of the drug.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-blood-flow-to-the-site-of-administration">2- Blood flow to the site of administration.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-blood-flow-to-the-site-of-administration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Rich blood supply (sublingual) enhances absorption whereas; poorly vascular site (subcutaneous) delays it.</p>
<p>For example, patient in shock may not respond to (IM) administration of drugs because of poor peripheral circulation.</p>
<p>N.B.: Drugs injected (IV) are placed directly into the circulatory system.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-solubility-of-the-drug">3- Solubility of the drug.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-solubility-of-the-drug" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>7</p>
<ul>
<li>In order to be absorbed drug must be in solution.</li>
<li>The more soluble the drug, the more rapidly it will be absorbed.</li>
</ul>
<p>N.B.: chemicals and minerals that form insoluble precipitates in the GIT or drugs that are insoluble in water or lipids can't be absorbed.</p>
<ul>
<li>Parenterally administered drugs prepared in oily vehicle will be more slowly absorbed than drugs dissolved in water or isotonic sodium chloride.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="4-influence-of-ph">4- Influence of pH:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-influence-of-ph" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Drugs that are acidic (e.g. Aspirin) become relatively undissociated in an acidic environment such as the stomach. And therefore can readily diffuse across the membrane into the circulation. In contrast, a basic</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>drug tends to ionize in the stomach acid environment and not absorbed through the gastric mucosa. The reverse occurs when the drugs are in an alkaline media.</p>
<p>N.B.: The unionized drug is lipid soluble readily diffuses across the cell membrane, the ionized drug is lipid insoluble and non-diffusable.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-drug-concentration">5- Drug concentration:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-drug-concentration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Drug administered in high concentration tend to be more rapidly absorbed than drugs administered in low concentration.</p>
<p>In certain situations, drug may be initially administered in large doses that temporarily exceed the body capacity for exertion of the drug. In this way the active drug levels are rapidly reached at the receptor site.</p>
<ul>
<li>Once active drug level is established by such cumulating effects, smaller doses of the drug can be administered to replace only the amount of the drug excreted since the previous dose.</li>
</ul>
<p>N.B. :- The initial dose temporary overloading doses of the drug are Priming or Loading doses, while the smaller daily doses are Maintenance dose</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dosage-form">Dosage form:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dosage-form" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>“Enteric coating” on drugs are used for the following reasons.</p>
<p>1- To prevent decomposition of chemically sensitive drugs to gastric secretions.
2- To prevent dilution of the drug before it reaches the intestine.
3- To prevent nausea and vomiting.
4- To provide delay action of the drug.</p>
<p>N.B.: Capsules forms are absorbed more rapidly than tablets because the powder inside capsules affords a large surface area than the compressed tablets.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="distribution">Distribution:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#distribution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Is defined as the transport of a drug in body fluids from the blood stream to various tissues of the body and ultimately to its site of action.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Most of drugs distributed initially to organs that have rich blood supply as the heart, liver and kidney. Delivery of the drug to the viscera, skin and adipose tissue is slower.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The distribution phase can be extremely slow for drugs that bind strongly to serum proteins, because the drug- protein complex is unable to pass out of the plasma.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>— Hypoalbuminemia, as in liver disease, burn and malnutrition may affect absorption and distribution of drugs.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Distribution barriers:-</p>
<p>Specialized structures which are made up of biologic membranes can serve as barriers to passage of drugs at certain sites in the body:</p>
<p>1- Blood- Brain Barrier: (BBB)</p>
<ul>
<li>Is a special anatomic arrangement that aims to distribute only lipids soluble drugs into the brain and CSF e.g. General anesthesia.</li>
<li>Ionized drugs &amp; poorly soluble in fat are not allowed to enter into the brain and CSF.</li>
<li>Antibiotics that cross the BBB with difficulty can NOT be used for CNS Infections such as meningitis and encephalities.</li>
<li>The instillation of the drug INTRATHECALY to bypass the BBB will provide direct effect against bacterial brain infection.</li>
</ul>
<p>2- Placental Barrier: (PB)
Is the membrane layers that separate the blood vessels of the mother and fetus.</p>
<p>N.B.: Tissue enzymes in the placenta have the ability to metabolize some agents (e.g. catecholamines) by inactivating them as they travel from maternal circulation to the embryo.</p>
<ul>
<li>Unlike BBB, the non-selective passage of drugs across the placenta to the fetus is well-established fact.</li>
</ul>
<p>2 major types of drug effects occur in the fetus:-
1- In the first trimester:
One type of drug may induce aberrant development of organs &amp; systems during the formation of these structures. This is known as a teratogenic drug which is defined as —An agent that causes physical defects in developing embryo.
2- The second type of drug affects the second half of pregnancy as well as delivery, when respiratory depression may occur in the newborn 10
because of its inability to biotransform &amp; excrete the drug given to the mother.</p>
<p>FDA Drug Categories:
Category A:
Adequate, well-controlled studies in pregnant women have not shown an increased risk of fetal abnormalities to the fetus in any trimester of pregnancy.</p>
<p>Category B:
Animal studies have revealed no evidence of harm to the fetus; however, there are no adequate and well-controlled studies in pregnant women.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>OR</p>
<p>Animal studies have shown as adverse effect, but adequate and wellcontrolled studies in pregnant women have failed to demonstrate a risk to the fetus in any trimester.</p>
<p>Category C:</p>
<p>Animal studies have shown an adverse effect and there are no adequate and well-controlled studies in pregnant women.</p>
<p>OR</p>
<p>No animal studies have been conducted and there are no adequate and wellcontrolled studies in pregnant women.</p>
<p>Category D:</p>
<p>Adequate well-controlled or observational studies in pregnant women have demonstrated a risk to the fetus.</p>
<p>However, the benefits of therapy may outweigh the potential risk. For example, the drug may be acceptable if needed in a life-threatening situation or serious disease for which safer drugs cannot be used or are ineffective.</p>
<p>Positive evidence of human fetal risk exists, but benefits in certain situations</p>
<p>"e.g. life-threatening situations or serious diseases" may make use of the drug acceptable despite its risks.</p>
<p>Category X:</p>
<p>Adequate well-controlled or observational studies in animals or pregnant women have demonstrated positive evidence of fetal abnormalities or risks. The use of the product is contraindicated in women who are or may become pregnant.</p>
<p>Studies in animals or humans have demonstrated fetal abnormalities, or there is evidence of fetal risk based on human experience, or both and the risk clearly outweighs any possible benefit.</p>
<p>Biotransformation "Metabolism"</p>
<p>Is a process that chemically inactivates a drug by converting it to a more soluble compound or metabolites for excretion from the body.</p>
<ul>
<li>Liver is the primary site of drug metabolism, but other tissues also may be involved in this process as plasma, kidney, lungs, and the intestinal mucosa.</li>
<li>Chemical alterations produced by microsomal enzyme system located largely in the liver.</li>
<li>By this process the drug is converted to more polar &amp; more water soluble.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>6</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>The process occurs by:-
1- Conjugation reaction: union of the polar group of a drug with another substance in the body. The conjugated molecule also
becomes more polar &amp; more water soluble, therefore more excretable.
2- Oxidation- reduction reaction:-
3- Hydrolysis</li>
<li>These responses generally produce a loss in pharmacological activity and occasionally are referred as DETOXIFICATION reactions.</li>
<li>N.B. :- Prolonged drugs metabolism may be expected in the following cases:-</li>
</ul>
<table><thead><tr><th>1-</th><th>Liver disease.</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>2-</td><td>Renal problems</td></tr><tr><td>3-</td><td>Sever cardiovascular dysfunction.</td></tr><tr><td>4-</td><td>Infant with immature metabolizing system.</td></tr><tr><td>5-</td><td>Aged with degenerative enzyme function.</td></tr><tr><td>-</td><td>Cumulative drug effects may be expected when drug metabolism is delayed which may be manifested as excessive or prolonged responses to ordinary doses of drug.</td></tr><tr><td>Excretion:</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Is the process by which drugs and pharmacologically active or inactive metabolites are eliminated from the body, so this process decreases the drug level in the body.</p>
<ul>
<li>The routes of elimination are:
1-Kidney: The majority of drugs and/or their metabolites are excreted through the urine.
2-Lung: The gases and volatile liquids, as general anesthetic, are excreted across the lung in the expired air.
3-Intestine: Many agents are eliminated through the intestine in the feces by biliary excretion.
4-Sweat and salivary glands (may cause skin rashes).
5-Mammary glands ... Transfer from mother to baby.
N.B. : Because of renal disease, the risk of drugs accumulation and drug toxicity is increased.
Note that dosage is reduced for most drugs in the presence of impaired renal function —some drugs can't be given|.
Onset of action:</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Reefers to the time interval between administration and notation of the first therapeutic effect. It depends on</p>
<p>1- The route of administration.
2- The characteristics of the drug.
3- The drug's rate of absorption through various membranes.
4- The formulation of the dose.</p>
<p>N.B.: The onset of action is especially variable after oral administration depending on the presence of food in the stomach, the motility of the GI tract and other factors.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="peak-of-activity">Peak of activity:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#peak-of-activity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When the drug reaches its maximum effect (coincides often with peak serum concentration). Many drugs cause this peak to surpass the optimally effective level but the concentration can fall rapidly below this level as a result of biotransformation and excretion. This drop occurs especially often when a short acting drug is given initially or intermittently.</p>
<p>Example: In treatment of diabetes, insulin with various lengths of action are mixed to keep insulin levels at a therapeutically effective level around the clock.</p>
<p>14</p>
<p>Duration: is the period between the administration of the drug and the excretion of the entire dose of that drug or its metabolites.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="bioavailability">Bioavailability:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bioavailability" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It measures the concentration of the pharmacologically active substance at the target site and / or in the serum.</p>
<p>It is the function of:</p>
<p>1- The drug itself.
2- The metabolism of the patient.
3- The rate at which the drug is liberated from its dosage form or from storage in the body.</p>
<p>Example: many drugs bind to serum protein (albumin) from which they released gradually, others stored at specific site as bone (tetracycline).</p>
<p>Drug isn't to be bioavailable if:</p>
<p>1- Bound to protein or to any other substance that makes the drug permanently or temporarily inactive.
2- Not released from its dosage form or site of administration.
3- Partially or totally degraded.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factors-that-influence-drug-dosage-and-action">Factors that influence drug dosage and action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-that-influence-drug-dosage-and-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is important for the nurse to be oriented of the characteristic that modify cell conditions and therefore modify the activity of a drug. These</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>characteristics include the following: -</p>
<p>1- Age:</p>
<ul>
<li>Children and elderly persons are highly responsive to drug.</li>
<li>Infants often have immature hepatic and renal systems and therefore incomplete metabolic &amp; excretory mechanisms.</li>
</ul>
<p>15</p>
<p>N.B.: Aged individuals may demonstrate different responses to drug therapy because of deterioration of hepatic and renal function which is often accompanied by concurrent disease process such as C.V.D. (cardiovascular disease).</p>
<p>2- Weight:</p>
<ul>
<li>The greater the weight, the greater must be the dose.</li>
<li>However, body weight due to fat or edema fluid should not be taken into consideration.</li>
<li>For very lean and very obese individuals, drug dosage is frequently determined on the basis of drug/kg of body weight or body surface area.</li>
</ul>
<p>3- Sex:</p>
<ul>
<li>Females don't always respond to the action of drug in the same manner as do men.</li>
<li>Women are usually smaller than men, which lead to high drug concentration if dosage is prescribed indifferently.</li>
<li>Female's body is composed of higher % of adipose tissue than males, absorption rate of drug are slower in fatty tissue than in skeletal muscle, so the effect of drug will be more pronounced and prolonged.</li>
</ul>
<p>N.B.: During pregnancy, lactation, and menstruation, many drugs are stopped:</p>
<ol>
<li>Aspirin: not used during menstruation as it increase blood fluidity.</li>
<li>Drugs excreted in milk aren't given during lactation as penicillin.</li>
<li>Uterine stimulant should be avoided during pregnancy as they may produce abortion such as prostaglandin.</li>
</ol>
<p>16</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Drugs that might affect fetus and placenta should not be given during pregnancy.</li>
</ol>
<p>4- Time of administration:</p>
<ul>
<li>Drug is more rapidly absorbed when the GIT is free of food, while irritating drugs are more tolerated if there is food in stomach.</li>
<li>Body resistant to drug is generally greater in the early morning when the body is at its lowest point of physiologic functioning and</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>conversely, the body is more sensitive to drugs effect during time of maximal activity.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-pathologic-state">5- Pathologic state :-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-pathologic-state" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Diseases alter the functional activity and accordingly its response to drug. e.g. sever pain tends to increase patient’s requirement to opiates.</li>
<li>The presence of circulatory, hepatic and/ or renal dysfunction will interfere with the physiologic process of drug action.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-environmental-milieu">6- Environmental Milieu:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-environmental-milieu" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Drugs affecting mood &amp; behavior are particularly susceptible to the influence of the patient’s environment.</li>
<li>With such drugs one has to consider effects in light of 4 FACTORS:-</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>The drug itself.</li>
<li>The personality of the user.</li>
<li>The environment of the user.</li>
<li>The interaction of these 3 components.</li>
<li>Heat relaxes peripheral blood vessels while cold has the opposite effect.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-genetic-factors">7- Genetic factors.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-genetic-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>17</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="channels-of-administration">Channels of Administration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#channels-of-administration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-the-oral-route-p-o">1- The ORAL route: (P.O.)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-the-oral-route-p-o" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>The first and most convenient method is the oral rout i.e. the patient usually swallows the drug, which then enters the gastrointestinal tract and absorbed from that area.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="advantages">Advantages:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>This route accounts for 80% of all medications administered to patients.</li>
<li>Doctors usually decide the amount and frequency and the patient administer the drug to himself.</li>
<li>The cost of medication and therapy is low.</li>
<li>Oral administration is painless and there is no necessity to practice sterile technique.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="disadvantages">Disadvantages:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Inconsistent absorption from the gastrointestinal tract.</li>
<li>Blood level may vary among different patients because of different GI characteristics e.g. acidity, gastric motility &amp; intestinal mucosa.</li>
<li>Drug irritation that causes nausea &amp; vomiting.</li>
<li>Unconscious patient &amp; vomiting patients can’t be given the drug</li>
</ul>

<p>by this route.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-parenteral-route">2- Parenteral Route:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-parenteral-route" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The next most popular route of drug administration.</li>
<li>The word parenteral indicates that the drug is administered by a route other than enteral route (GI).</li>
<li>Common agreement has come to indicate the injectable route.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages">Advantages:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Drugs that cannot be given through GIT, can be given by parenteraly.</li>
</ul>
<p>18</p>
<ul>
<li>Eliminate the unpredictability of absorption from GIT i.e. the amount of drug will be delivered to the patient from injection site.</li>
<li>Medication can be given to an unconscious patient.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages">Disadvantages:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Need sterile technique.</li>
<li>More expensive than oral preparations.</li>
<li>Patient usually not able to medicate himself especially when medication needs to be injected deep into a muscle.</li>
<li>Accidental penetration of blood vessel, especially if medication is not suitable for I.V. administration (complication).</li>
</ul>
<p>There are a number of techniques for administering drugs by injection, these are related to the target area of the injection:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-subcutaneous-injection">A. Subcutaneous Injection:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-subcutaneous-injection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>SC injection is administration of a drug into the subcutaneous tissues.</p>
<ul>
<li>Slowly drug absorption (advantage)</li>
<li>Disadvantages:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>The most painful route.</li>
<li>Slow rate of absorption.</li>
<li>Not effective in emergency (poor blood supply).</li>
</ol>
<p>N.B.: Drug absorption from SC injection can be reduced by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Addition of vasoconstrictor e.g. epinephrine.</li>
<li>Application of cold packs (also causes vasoconstriction).</li>
<li>Heat causes vasodilation which result in increased blood supply to the area and thus quicker drug absorption.</li>
<li>This manipulation may be used to reduce the severity of toxicity from a SC injection.</li>
</ul>
<p>19</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-intramuscular-route-im">A. Intramuscular Route: IM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-intramuscular-route-im" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Is the second most widely used route for injectable drugs.</li>
<li>Suitable for administration of both solutions and suspensions.</li>
<li>Drugs that are very water insoluble can be given IM in an oil base.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>(Remain for an extended period of time).</p>
<ul>
<li>Has greater vascular network than SC, so drug absorption is more quickly than SC route.</li>
<li>Less painful (less nerve supply).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-intravenous-injection-iv">B. Intravenous Injection: IV<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-intravenous-injection-iv" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Administering a quantity of medication through a needle into the circulation.</li>
<li>2 methods of intravenous injection are used:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Administering the drug as a bolus.</li>
<li>Continuous infusion of a drug, which is called IV drip.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages">Advantages:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1- To achieve highly, accurate and quick blood level.
2- A channel to administer drugs that irritate another sites e.g. chemotherapy.
3- Less painful during drug administration.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages">Disadvantages:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Accidental overdose, and there is no way to withdraw the drug from circulation once it is injected.</li>
<li>Infiltrating the area around the vein i.e. needle slip out of the vein.</li>
</ol>
<p>20</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Thrombophlebitis from repeated injections. To minimize this phenomena (but doesn't exclude it), drug should be given I.V. drip.</li>
<li>Inadvertent intra-arterial injection instead of a vein.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="n-b">N.B.:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#n-b" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>IV solutions must be completely homogenous. No solution containing particulate matter, regardless of how fine the particles should ever be injected IV because of the danger of creating EMBLOI.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-intradermal-id-and-intrathecal-administration">C. Intradermal (ID) and Intrathecal administration:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-intradermal-id-and-intrathecal-administration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>ID is a route of administration in which the drug is injected just below the epidermis.</li>
<li>Injection is usually used for allergy test.</li>
<li>Used for TB tests and for penicillin sensitivity test.</li>
<li>Intrathecal route of administration involves inserting a needle between 2 vertebrae and injecting the drug into the CSF.</li>
<li>Used frequently in OR when anesthesiologist desires to produce a spinal block and inject local anesthetic directly into the spinal cord. Used to administer Chemotherapy to prevent CNS metastases of some types of cancers.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
5 studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>D. Rectal, urethral and vaginal suppositories:</p>
<p>Another route of administration that is useful when:</p>
<ul>
<li>The oral route can't be used.</li>
<li>The physician desires not to use the injectable route or.</li>
<li>When self-medication other than P.O. is desired, the rectal route of administration is used.</li>
</ul>
<p>N.B.: rectal route can produce local effect or systemic effect.</p>
<p>21</p>
<p>Disadvantages:</p>
<ul>
<li>Erratic absorption from the rectal area result in an inaccurate predicted blood level of drug so the dosage must be adjusted.</li>
<li>Rectal route is ineffective when the patient suffers from diarrhea.</li>
</ul>
<p>Examples:-
Rectal supp. ___ used to treat hemorrhoids.
Vaginal supp. ___ used to treat vaginitis.
Urethral supp. ___ used to treat bladder conditions.</p>
<p>E. Topical route:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Are intended for use at the site of administration (there are exceptions e.g. Nitroglycerin ointment that is rubbed into the skin and systemic effect is achieved.</li>
<li>Two topical preparations are frequently confused with each other (ointment and creams).</li>
</ul>
<p>1- Ointments:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Are usually made up of a petrolatum type of base.</li>
<li>They are quite greasy, as they intended for prolonged contact with the skin.</li>
<li>They don't disappear or penetrate the skin, but remain on the surface.</li>
</ul>
<p>2- Creams:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Made of viscous water-soluble chemicals, which usually disappear after being placed to the skin.</li>
<li>Patient prefers cream to ointment, as creams don't discolor clothing.</li>
</ul>
<p>Naming of drugs:-
1- Generic name: (chemical name), defines the chemical structure.</p>
<p>22</p>
<p>2- Trade name: is given by specific pharmaceutical company.</p>
<p>How do drugs work?
&gt; In spite of a great deal of research, it is still not known how some drugs produce their effect, but it is possible to describe</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>the way in which some of them act.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-the-receptor-theory">1- The receptor theory:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-the-receptor-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is believed that the cells in certain tissues contain structures (called receptors). These receptors combine with substances, which are produced naturally in the body.</li>
<li>The drugs stimulate the receptors which will cause the cells to be stimulated.</li>
<li>The contraction of muscle fibers produced by acetylcholine is an example.</li>
<li>The drug is thought to fit into a receptor rather as a key fits into a lock. It will then stimulate the receptor and produce an effect similar to that of the naturally occurring substance or it may occupy (block) the receptor without producing any effect but preventing any naturally occurring stimulation to happen (the blocking of acetylcholine by atropine is a good example).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-antimetabolites">2- Antimetabolites:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-antimetabolites" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>These drugs closely resemble substances which are used by the cells for nutrition and when absorbed, the cells cannot use them and so fail to multiply.</li>
<li>The Sulfonamides, which are used to stop the multiplication of bacteria, are a good example.</li>
</ul>
<p>23</p>
<ul>
<li>They are very similar in structure to para-aminobenzoic acid and certain bacteria can't distinguish between them, and absorb the sulfonamide so multiplication is stopped.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-enzyme-inhibitors">3- Enzyme Inhibitors:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-enzyme-inhibitors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Enzymes are substances that speed up many chemical processes within the body.</li>
<li>Some of these enzyme-activated processes are concerned with the transport of chemicals in and out of the cells. Certain drugs have the property of inhibiting their action and thus interfere with some of these processes.</li>
<li>Diuretics are a good example as normally salt and water is transported out of the renal tubule back into the body, but this action requires enzymes and if they are inhibited by a diuretic, salt and water are not reabsorbed and pass out of the kidney with a resulting diuresis.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-action-on-cell-membranes">4- Action on cell membranes:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-action-on-cell-membranes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The function of nerves and muscles depends on ions passing across the membranes surrounding these cells.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-cytotoxic-effect">5-Cytotoxic Effect:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-cytotoxic-effect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Drugs may be used to kill bacteria or malignant cells without undue damage to the patient’s cells. The way this is brought about varies between drugs.</p>
<p>These are just a few of the ways in which drugs may work. It is probable that all drug action depends on their interference with cell activity and</p>
<p>24</p>
<p>when more is known about the processes within the cell, then more will be discovered about how do drugs work.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects-and-drug-toxicity">Side effects and drug toxicity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-and-drug-toxicity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-drug-allergies">A. Drug Allergies:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-drug-allergies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Allergic responses to drugs occur in some patients and not in others.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> It is an unwanted response to a drug resulting from previous exposure to that drug or one closely related to it. So drug allergy is happens only after a second or subsequent exposure to the drug.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Allergic reactions to drugs differ from drug toxicity in the following ways.</p>
<ol>
<li>The allergic reaction occurs in only a fraction of the population where as toxicity will occur in all individuals if the dose is high enough.</li>
<li>The allergic response is unusual in that a small amount of unsafe drug causes a severe reaction.</li>
<li>With allergy, the reaction is different from the usual pharmacological effect of the drug.</li>
<li>For an allergic reaction to occur, the patient must have had a previous exposure to that drug or one closely related to it.</li>
</ol>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> There are 2 types of allergic responses:</p>
<ol>
<li>Immediate reaction involving antigen and antibody resulting in the release of histamine.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>In mild cases, the reaction is limited to urticaria (wheals and itching of the skin).</li>
<li>In severe cases (anaphylactic reaction), characterized by circulatory collapse or asphyxia due to swelling of the larynx &amp; occlusion of the air way passages.</li>
</ul>
<p>25</p>
<ul>
<li>Example: many patients are allergic to penicillin.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Delayed reaction:</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Occurring several days or even weeks after the drug has been administered.</li>
<li>Characterized by fever (drug fever), swelling of the joints, reaction may involves blood-forming organs and kidneys.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-anaphylactic-reaction-may-include-administration-of">Treatment of anaphylactic reaction may include administration of:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-anaphylactic-reaction-may-include-administration-of" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1- Epinephrine
2- Oxygen
3- Antihistamines
4- Corticosteroids</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-drug-idiosyncrasies">B. Drug idiosyncrasies:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-drug-idiosyncrasies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; Idiosyncratic reactions are defined as those reactions that occur in patients who have abnormal genes which cause this abnormal response to that drug. Reaction may be excessive and unusual.
&gt; Example: Succinylcholine, a muscle relaxant drug, usually is broken down rapidly by enzymes in the plasma and liver so that the effects of the drug last for only a few minutes. In few patients, a normal dose of this drug produces profound muscle relaxation and suppression of respiration, which may last few hours. Those patients have a genetic defect that produces unusual enzymes &amp; the drug is not broken down.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-drug-hypersensitivity">C. Drug Hypersensitivity:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-drug-hypersensitivity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; It occurs when the patient shows extreme sensitivity to an effect of the drug. The response is the usual pharmacological effect, however the effect is intense and exaggerated. A simple decrease in the dose may be sufficient to eliminate this type of reactions.</p>
<p>26</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="d-drug-toxicity">D. Drug toxicity:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-drug-toxicity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; Excess dosage may be either accidental or intentional, results in an exaggerated response to this drug. It may be sever &amp; may lead to respiratory depression. Cardio-vascular collapse and death may occur if the drug is not withdrawn and adequate treatment is started.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="e-general-side-effects">E. General side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#e-general-side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; Unpleasant or unwanted reaction to a drug is termed as side-effects.</p>
<ul>
<li>Dermatologic reactions — pruritis, urticaria, alopecia, granulomas, rashes, photosensitivity,……</li>
<li>Blood dyscrasias: in certain patients, bone marrow is sensitive to certain drugs; this may result in the insufficient production of platelets, red blood cells &amp; white blood cells.
&gt; N.B.: Patients who receive a drug that may cause bone-marrow depression are monitored closely by frequent blood counts &amp; for early signs &amp; symptoms of infection.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
5 studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>&gt; Some forms of blood dyscrasias:
1- Agranulocytosis (reduction in the number of granulocytes).</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>2- Aplastic anemia elements of blood).</th><th>Pancytopnea (reduction of all formed</th></tr></thead></table>
<p>3- Hemolytic anemia (reduced hemoglobin level due to lyses of RBCs).
4- Thrombocytopnea. (platelets deficiency) hemorrhage.
&gt; Hepatotoxicity. (Liver damage) Abdominal pain &amp; jaundice.
&gt; Nephrotoxicity. (Kidney damages) hematuria, anuria, proteinuria, edema &amp; uremia.
&gt; Ototoxicity (ear damage) damage of vestibular or/and auditory portion of the 8th cranial nerve.</p>
<p>27</p>
<p>&gt; CNS toxicity loss of judgment, loss of movement coordination, loss of consciousness, convulsions, tardive dyskinesia, reduce kneejerk reflex, drowsiness, dizziness, ...
&gt; GI disturbance nausea, vomiting, abdominal pain, diarrhea...
&gt; Sexual dysfunction change in libido.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="drugs-orders-and-prescriptions">Drugs orders and prescriptions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drugs-orders-and-prescriptions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="prescription">Prescription:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prescription" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>&gt; Medicating a patient begins when the medication is suggested and authorized by a legal prescriber, usually a licensed physician, dentist or veterinarian.
&gt; It consists of 4 parts:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-the-superscription">1. The superscription:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-the-superscription" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>☑ It includes the patient’s name, address, date and the symbol Rx.
☑ The age of an infant or a child should be written to permit the pharmacist to check the correctness of the dose.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-the-inscription">2. The inscription:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-the-inscription" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>☑ It states the name of the drug, dosage form, and the amount.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-the-subscription">3. The subscription:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-the-subscription" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>☑ It contains the directions of the pharmacist, now usually limited to the number of the doses to be dispensed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="4-the-signature">4. The signature:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-the-signature" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>☑ It is abbreviated by —S|| or —Sig||
☑ It includes the prescriber’s signature.</p>
<p>On the other hand the prescriber’s order has several elements that should be presented and identified:-
1- Patient’s name and other identifying data.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>2- Date that the order was written.</p>
<p>28</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>3-</th><th>Medication name.</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>4-</td><td>Dosage to be administered each time.</td></tr><tr><td>5-</td><td>Route of administration.</td></tr><tr><td>6-</td><td>Frequency of administration and special instructions.</td></tr><tr><td>7-</td><td>Prescriber’s signature.</td></tr><tr><td>☑ Example :</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Name : Ahmad mohammad</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Address: Gaza, Tofah</td><td>Age: 20 years</td></tr><tr><td>Date: 15/1/2012</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Rx</p>
