<p>Signature</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-orders">Types of orders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-orders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; It is probably obvious, that outpatients are free to medicate themselves with any accessible medication. Many Over the Counter (OTC) drugs are available for the public without the need for a prescription.</p>
<p>&gt; Once an individual is admitted to a clinical institution, usually neither the patient nor the nurse may legally administer any medication without a written order.</p>
<p>&gt; Use of variant or non-standard abbreviations should be avoided because of the danger of misinterpretation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-routine-order">1. Routine Order:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-routine-order" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; The most common type of orders. It means that the drug, as ordered, is to be regularly administered until a formal discontinuation order is written, or until a specified termination date is reached.</p>
<p>&gt; Automatic termination or stop may be explicit in agency policy; e.g. narcotic analgesics 3 days, Antibiotics 5 days, steroids 7 days ………</p>
<p>&gt; The policies act as a stimulus to the prescriber to evaluate continued need for these drugs that require especial close attention.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-single-order">2. Single Order:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-single-order" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; Drug is to be administered once at the time indicated.</p>
<p>&gt; e.g. a preoperative medication (Atropine) 0.4 mg IM on call to OR.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-stat-order">3. Stat Order:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-stat-order" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; This is a single order that a drug is to be administered immediately. Stat orders are written often for emergency when the client’s condition changes suddenly.</p>
<p>&gt; Example: Give Aprisoline 10 mg IM stat.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>prn Orders:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>These drugs are to be administered by the nurse as necessary within the order criteria specified by the doctor order. The decision of when to give the drug is left to the nurse’s judgment.</li>
<li>Medications to reduce the perception of pain make up the bulk of prn orders.</li>
<li>Keeping nursing assessment of the pain is required to carry out these prn orders appropriately.</li>
<li>The PQRST method is one that may be used to help the nurse in asking the patient questions to get helpful information:</li>
</ul>
<p>P ... Precipitating &amp; palliating factors —what brings &amp; what relief it
Q ... Quality of the pain —how would you describe the pain, burning, stabbing, squeezing...
R ... Region &amp; Radiation —where is the pain ...
S ... Severity.
T ... Time factor ... How does the pain occur, How long does it last.</p>
<p>30</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Telephone order and verbal order:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Usually given in emergency and should be written in the patient’s chart and assigned by the nurse who receive the order and to be signed by doctor as soon as possible.</li>
<li>Example: 10:15 am, diclofine 50 mg IM stat, Phone order Dr. Ahmad Attallah to Nurse Sami Mahmoud. Then the nurse sings his/her name</li>
<li>Disadvantages :-</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Forgotten if not written at that time.</li>
<li>It is illegal until the order is signed for by the prescriber (depending on the hospital policy).</li>
<li>Can easily be mis-communicated, misinterpreted or not clearly heard.</li>
</ol>
<p>General Guidelines for Handling Medications</p>
<ol>
<li>When preparing or giving medicines, concentrate your whole attention on what you are doing.</li>
<li>Make certain that you have a written order for every medication you will administer.</li>
<li>Read the label before taking, while using, and returning the drug to its place.</li>
<li>All medicines should be labeled and the label should be clear.</li>
<li>Never give medicine from unlabeled container.</li>
<li>Never give a put a drug in a bottle that has a different label. For example, if you have kefex that you need to put it in a bottle, and you</li>
</ol>
<p>have empty bottle that was used to contain ampecillin, don't put the keflex in that bottle.</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>Measure quantities and calculate doses as ordered in proper way.</li>
</ol>
<p>31</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>
<p>Handling tablets, capsules and pills properly and DO'NOT touch with fingers. Use the cap of the container to guide or from the container to the cup directly.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Avoid wastage of medicine.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Never administer medications prepared by another person; otherwise you will bear the responsibility of any mistake.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Some preparations as insulin, vaccines &amp; suppositories need to be kept in the refrigerator —2-8° C|.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stay with the patient until he takes his medicine.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>All mixtures should be made immediately before use.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>NEVER return unused drug to a stock bottle.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Don't add any drug to the blood; interactions may occur without visible changes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Don't use any sterile article that gets unsterile by any way.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Don't use clear solutions which have become cloudy or have sediment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Don't use a drug that is out date.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Don't use a drug that has changes its color.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Don't use a drug which arise doubt in mind.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>All medicines should be kept in cupboard, NARCOTICS in a locked one.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Narcotics have a rule controlling their ordering, giving, and their registration.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Many liquids should be diluted with water or other liquids. —This is especially when medicine has a bad taste|.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Exceptions to this rule, cough medicines are not diluted, or the patient not allowed drinking water after taking cough syrup.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>32</p>
<ol start="25">
<li>
<p>Don't leave a tray of medicines unattended. If you are in a patient's room and must leave, take the tray with you.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Never chart a medicine as having been given, until it has been administered.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Follow up the five rights</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right patient.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right drug.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right dose.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right route of administration.</p>
</li>
</ol>

<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Tolerance = Decrease physiologic response to the repeated administration of a drug or chemically related substances which necessities increase in dosage to maintain a given therapeutic effect e.g. morphine.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Dependence (addiction): When the body is getting used to function in the presence of a certain drug. The body will not perform its normal functions in the absence of that drug.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Substitute = these are many different drugs which may used to treat a single disease. From these drugs, always present a drug of choice, if not available the others are considered as the substitute.
&gt; Antidote = a drug used to antagonize the toxic effect of another drug and to neutralize its symptoms.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1b7f4715">Anti – infectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1b7f4715" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; The beginning of modern medicine is generally related to 2 events:
&gt; 1- The proof by Pasteur that many diseases are caused by microorganisms.
&gt; 2- The discovery of effective anti-infective drugs.
&gt; • sulfonamides (1938).
&gt; • Penicillin (1940).
&gt;
&gt; Some of the bacteria and other microorganisms have adapted to the anti-infectives and became resistant to certain antibiotics.
&gt;
&gt; Most resistant strains can be eradicated by:
&gt; 1- New and/or different antibiotics.
&gt; 2- Antibiotic combinations.
&gt; 3- Higher dosages.</p>
<p>35</p>
<p>&gt; Awareness of the problem has prompted somewhat greater scrutiny by the physician as to when and how to prescribe antibiotics.
&gt;
&gt; Anti-infective drugs can be divided into:-
&gt; 1- Bacteriostatic: Stop the multiplication and further development of the infectious agent.
&gt; 2- Bactericidal: eradicate (kill) all living</p>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>microorganisms.</p>
<p>&gt; Some anti-infectives halt the growth or eradicate many different microorganism are termed as <strong>broad-spectrum antibiotics</strong>.
&gt; Others affect only certain specific organisms and are termed <strong>narrow-spectrum antibiotics</strong>.
&gt; Some of anti-infectives elicit a hypersensitivity reaction in some persons. Some Penicillins cause more sever &amp; more frequent hypersensitivity reactions than other drugs.
&gt; <strong>Antibiotics</strong> = drugs produced by microorganisms or other live organisms to kill other microorganisms. Nowadays, many are produced synthetically.
&gt; Because of differences in susceptibility of infectious agent to antiinfectives, the sensitivity of the microorganism to the drug ordered should be determined before treatment is initiated. Several sensitivity tests are commonly used for this purpose; e.g. (Culture and sensitivity).
&gt; Certain anti-infectives have marked side-effects (some are serious) e.g. neurotoxicity, nephrotoxicity &amp; ototoxicity.
&gt; Another difficulty is that these drugs can eradicate the normal flora in the intestine which are necessary for proper digestion, synthesis of vitamin K and control of fungi that may gain access to the GIT (super infection).
&gt; Uses of anti-infectives:</p>
<p><strong>A: Prophylactic</strong></p>
<p>1- To protect persons exposed to a known specific organism.
2- To inhibit spread of infection from a clearly defined focus as after surgery or accidents.
3- To sterilize the bowel or other areas of the body in preparation for extensive surgery.</p>
<p><strong>B. Acute infections:</strong> antibiotics are used to treat acute infections such as tonsillitis and acute upper respiratory tract infections.</p>
<p>&gt; <strong>Contraindication:</strong> allergy or hypersensitivity reaction.</p>
<p>&gt; <strong>Drug considerations:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Check expiration date on the container.</li>
<li>Check for recommended method of storage and reconstitution.</li>
<li>Clear mark the date &amp; time of reconstitution, your initials and the strength of the solutions of all drugs.</li>
<li>Note the length of time that the drug may be stored after dilution and store under appropriate condition.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="penicillins">Penicillins<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#penicillins" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>&gt; Class: Anti-infective.
&gt; Action: Inhibit cell wall synthesis, they inhibit cell division &amp; growth.</p>
<ul>
<li>It is bactericidal &amp; bacteriostatic —according to concentration of drug and microorganism|.</li>
</ul>
<p>37</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>It is most effective against young, rapidly dividing organisms; therefore, they are not used for bacteria in resting phase.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They diffuse well into body tissues and fluids.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They are excreted in the urine in the therapeutic concentration.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They do not kill bacteria in the resting phase.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Uses:</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Gram +ve cocci —streptococci, meningococci, pneumococci ...||</li>
<li>Subacute bacterial endocarditis caused by group A streptococci.</li>
<li>Gonorrhea due to gonococci.</li>
<li>Diphtheria, tetanus, anthrax, gas gangrene.</li>
<li>Prophylaxis for rheumatic fever.</li>
</ol>
<p>&gt; Note: Not all penicillins are used for the above diseases. Specific uses are indicated for each of the individually listed drugs.</p>
<p>&gt; Contraindications:
&gt; Hypersensitivity to penicillins &amp; cephalosporins.</p>
<p>&gt; Side effects:</p>
<ul>
<li>Allergy skin rashes, pruritis, wheezing, fever... .</li>
<li>Diarrhea, abdominal cramps\pain, nausea, vomiting.</li>
<li>Psendomembranous colitis, thrombocytopnea, leukopenia</li>
<li>Thrombophlebitis + Electrolytes imbalance following I.V. use.</li>
<li>Hepatotoxicity.</li>
<li>I.M. injection may cause pain at the injection site.</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; N.B.: Emergency treatment of allergy includes:</p>
<ol>
<li>epinephrine</li>
<li>corticosteroids</li>
<li>oxygen</li>
</ol>
<p>38</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>antihistamines</li>
</ol>
<p>&gt; Dosage: Individualized.</p>
<p>&gt; General Nursing considerations for penicillin:</p>
<ol>
<li>These antibiotics should be injected slowly to minimize local irritation.</li>
<li>I.M. injections are made deeply into the gluteal muscle.</li>
<li>Assess regularly for allergic reactions. If reaction occurs the</li>
</ol>
<p>This document is available on
s
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>drug must be discontinued immediately, Epinephrine, O₂, antihistamines, &amp; corticosteroids must be immediately available.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>keep client who received penicillin in outpatient clinics to stay in the clinic for at least 20 minute after administering Penicillin</li>
<li>Don't administer long-acting types I.V., they are only for I.M. use &amp; don't massage after injection because rate of absorption should not be increased.</li>
<li>Take oral penicillin 1 hr before or 2-3 hr after meals.</li>
<li>Complete entire prescribed course of therapy.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-ampicillin">1) Ampicillin:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-ampicillin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Trade name: Penbritin.</li>
<li>Class: Antibiotic, penicillin.</li>
<li>Notes: Destroyed by penicillinase (lactamase enzymes)</li>
<li>30-60% absorbed from GIT after oral use.</li>
<li>Acid resistant.</li>
<li>Broad – spectrum antibiotic.</li>
<li>Uses: Is particularly recommended in respiratory, urinary &amp; GI tract infections &amp; other infections due to ampicillin sensitive organisms.</li>
</ul>
<p>39</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dosage-forms">Dosage forms:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dosage-forms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Capsules 250 mg, suspension 125 mg/5ml, vials 250, 500, 1000 mg.</li>
<li>Ampecilin forte capsules 500 mg, ampecillin forte suspension 250 mg/5ml.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dosage">Dosage:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dosage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>P.O., I.V. or I.M. 250 mg – 500 mg q 6 hr (adult).</li>
<li>Children 50 mg/kg 1 day in 4 divided doses.</li>
<li>N.B. For bacterial meningitis</li>
<li>Adults: 12gm are given in divided doses (3 gm q 6 hr).</li>
<li>Children: up to 400 mg/kg daily in divided doses q 4 hr.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="specific-nursing-considerations">Specific nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#specific-nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>After reconstitution for I.M., I.V. administration, the solution must be used within the hour.</li>
<li>I.V. administration, should be given slowly within 3-5 minutes or by infusion.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-penicillin-g-benzathine-and-procaine-combined">5) Penicillin G, Benzathine and procaine combined:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-penicillin-g-benzathine-and-procaine-combined" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Shake multiple-dose vial vigorously before withdrawing the desired dose.</li>
<li>Use a 20- gauge needle &amp; don’t allow medication to remain in the syringe &amp; needle for long periods of time before administration because the needle may become plugged &amp; the syringe —frozen.</li>
<li>Inject slowly into the muscle &amp; don’t massage the injection site.</li>
<li>Before injection of medication, aspirate needle to ascertain that needle is not in a vein.</li>
<li>Rotate site of injections.</li>
<li>Don’t administer IV.</li>
<li>If dose is large and the available muscle is small, divide the dose</li>
</ul>

<li>Penicillin G Sodium "for injection": [Benzylpenicillin Na].</li>

<p>&gt; Trade name: Crystapen, crystalline penicillin.
Penicillin G potassium "oral" + Injection [Benzylpenicillin k]
&gt; Trade name: Megacillin.
&gt; Class: Antibiotic, penicillin.</p>
<p>43</p>
<p>&gt; N.B.: The low cost of penicillin G still makes it the first choice for treatment of many infections.
&gt; Rapid onset makes it especially suitable for fulminating infections.
&gt; Destroyed by acid &amp; penicillinase.

<li>Rapid I.V. administration may cause hyperkalemia &amp; cardiac arrhythmias.</li>
<li>Thrombophlebitis, so assess the site of administration before administering each dose.
&gt; Uses: Infections due to penicillin- sensitive organisms.
&gt; N.B.: Penicillin G potassium is indicated as on alternative to penicillin G sodium in those patients in whom intake of sodium must be restricted.
&gt; Contraindications: Hypersensitivity.
&gt; Dosage forms: Penicillin G potassium (injection) vial of 1 MU and Penicillin G sodium vials of 1,5,10 Mu.
&gt; Dosage: I.M., continuous I.V. infusion 300,000 – 30 million unit depending on the use.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cephalosporins">Cephalosporins<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cephalosporins" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Are semisynthetic antibiotics that resemble the penicillins both chemically and pharmacologically.</li>
<li>Are absorbed rapidly from the GI tract and quickly reach effective concentrations in the urinary, GI and respiratory tracts except in patients with pernicious anemia or obstructive jaundice &amp; eliminated rapidly in patients with normal renal function.</li>
<li>They are broad-spectrum antibiotics that have been classified as first, second and third generation drugs. The difference among generations is based on antibacterial spectra.</li>
<li>Third generation cephalosporins have more activity against gram negative organisms and resistant organisms &amp; less activity against gram positive organisms than first generation drugs. They are also stable against beta-lactamase enzymes.</li>
<li>The cost increases from 1st to 3rd generation cephalosporins.</li>
<li><strong>Action</strong>: They interfere with the final step in the formation of the bacterial cell wall resulting in unstable cell membranes that undergo lysis, also cell division &amp; growth are inhibited.</li>
</ul>
<p>45</p>
<ul>
<li>N.B.: 1st &amp; 2nd generation drugs don't enter the CSF well, but 3rd generation drugs enter inflamed meninges readily.</li>
<li>Cephabsporins are excreted rapidly by the kidneys.</li>
<li><strong>Uses</strong>: They are effective against infections of:
1- Biliary tract
2- BI tract
3- GU tract
4- Bones &amp; joints
5- Upper &amp; lower respiratory tract
6- Skin
7- Meningitis
8- Osteomyelitis
9- Peritonitis
10- Otitis media
11- Gonorrhea
12- Prophylaxis prior to surgery.</li>
<li><strong>Contraindications</strong>: Hypersensitivity to cephalosporins or Penicillin, renal failure, Pregnancy, Lactation.</li>
<li><strong>Side effects</strong>:</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Nausea, vomiting, diarrhea, anorexia, abdominal pain, flatulence, skin rashes, super-infection, heartburn, sore mouth, bone marrow depression: (Decrease WBC, decreased platelets, decreased Hct), Nephrotoxicity, (pain, abscess at injection site, phlebitis and inflammation at IV site).</p>
<p><strong>Drug considerations:-</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Infuse over 30 minutes unless otherwise indicated.</li>
</ul>
<p>46</p>
<ul>
<li>Therapy should be continued for at least 2-3 days after symptoms of infection have disappeared.</li>
<li>Assess client with a history of hypersensitivity reaction. —for penicillin or cephalosporins.</li>
<li>Assess client financial status. These drugs are usually expensive.</li>
<li>If GI upset occurs administer drugs with meals. —Should be administered on empty stomach.</li>
<li>Obtain liver &amp; renal studies.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Examples:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Cephalexin monohydrate:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Trade names: Keflex, Jeflex.</li>
<li>Class.: antibiotic, cephalosporin (first generation).</li>
<li>Uses: infections of respiratory tract, skin, bones &amp; GU.</li>
<li>Additional Side-effects: Nephrotoxicity, jaundice.</li>
<li>Dosage: caps., suspension, tab. 250-500 mg q 6 hr.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Cephalothin sodium:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Trade name: Keflin.</li>
<li>Class: Antibiotic, cephalosporin (first generation).</li>
<li>N.B.: poorly absorbed from GI tract &amp; must be given parenterally.</li>
<li>Dosage: Deep I.M. or I.V. 500-1000 mg a 4-6 hr.</li>
<li>Uses: see Keflex.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Cefaclor:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Trade name: ceclor</li>
<li>Classification: antibiotic, cephalosporin — second generation</li>
</ul>
<p>47</p>
<ul>
<li>Uses: otitis media, infections of upper &amp; lower respiratory tract. UTI &amp; skin infections.</li>
<li>Dosage: Capsules, oral suspension. 250 mg every 8 hr &amp; may be doubled in case of severe infection (for adults). Children 20 mg/kg/day in 3 divided doses.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-cefuroxime-sodium">4. Cefuroxime Sodium:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-cefuroxime-sodium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-cefixime-oral">5. Cefixime, oral:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-cefixime-oral" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>Trade name: suprax.</li>
<li>Classification: antibiotic, cephalosporin (third generation).</li>

<li>Uses: Uncomplicated UTI, pharyngitis, tonsillitis &amp; acute bronchitis.</li>
<li>Additional side effects: Flatulence, alkaline phosphatase levels.</li>
</ul>
<p>48</p>
<ul>

<li>Therapy should be taken once a day at the same time each day.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-cefotaxime-sodium">6. Cefotaxime Sodium:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-cefotaxime-sodium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

&gt; Drug considerations:-</p>

<li>Should not be mixed with aminoglycosides. (each should be given separately)</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-ceftriaxone-soduim">7. Ceftriaxone Soduim:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-ceftriaxone-soduim" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

&gt; Drug considerations:-</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aminoglycosides">Aminoglycosides<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aminoglycosides" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Are broad-spectrum antibiotics primarily used for the treatment of serious gram negative infection caused by Pseudomonas, E.coli, proteus and klebsiella.</li>
<li>It distributed in extracellular fluids, cross the placenta barriers but not the BBB because it isn't lipid-soluble.</li>
<li>Are excreted largely in the urine, so it is suitable for urinary tract infections.</li>
<li>Are powerful antibiotics that can induce serious side effects.</li>
</ul>
<p>50</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="action">Action:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>They are believed to inhibit protein synthesis by binding irreversibly to ribosome which leads to production of nonfunctional protein.
They are usually bactericidal as a result of disruption of bacterial cytoplasmic membrane.</p>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>They are poorly absorbed from the GI tract, therefore are usually administered parenterally, not orally.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Uses:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Gram negative bacteria causing:</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Bone and joint infections.</li>
<li>Respiratory tract infections.</li>
<li>Septicemia (including neonatal sepsis).</li>
<li>Urinary tract infection (UIT).</li>
<li>Post operative infections.</li>
<li>Intra-abdominal infections (as peritonitis).</li>
<li>Skin infections (including burns).
N.B.: It should be used for gram +ve bacteria only when other less toxic drugs either ineffective or contraindicated.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Contraindications:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hypersensitivity to aminoglycosides.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Long-term therapy —except streptomycin for tuberculosis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>For patients with impaired renal function or pre-existing hearing impairment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Side effects</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Ototoxicity: tinnitis, hearing impairment, ataxia &amp; dizziness.</li>
<li>Renal impairment (Nephrotoxicity) hematuria, proteinuria...51</li>
<li>Neurotoxicity: headache, tremor, lethargy, numbness, burning of face.</li>
<li>Others: nausea, vomiting, skin rash &amp; super infection.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Drug interactions:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vancomycin additive: ototoxicity &amp; nephrotoxicity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Penicillin decrease the effect of aminoglycosides.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Drug considerations:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Assess history of hypersensitivity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>See anti-infectives.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>IM administration inject deep into muscle to minimize pain.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Administer for only 7-10 days.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Obtain laboratory studies for renal function.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Continue to monitor for ototoxicity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Discuss with the client / family the importance of taking medications at the appropriate prescribed time intervals.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Examples:</p>
<ol>
<li>Amikacin Sulfate:
&gt; Trade name: Amikin.</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-gentamycin-sulfate">2. <p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Trade name: Garamyein.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Class: antibiotic, aminoglycosides.</p>

<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Dose: adults: 3 mg/kg/day divided into equal 3 doses q 8 hrs IV or IM.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> N.B. It is the drug of choice for hospital-acquired gram negative sepsis including neonatal sepsis.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Serious staphylococcal infections.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Side effects:</p>
<ul>
<li>Alopecia</li>
<li>CNS: ototoxicity, neurotoxicity, tenitis, dizziness, ringing in the ears, vertigo.</li>
<li>GI: nausea, vomiting, anorexia, weight loss, increased salivation.</li>
<li>C.V.: palpitation, hypotensioin or hypertension.</li>
<li>Hematologic: Decrease number of blood cells.</li>
<li>GU: nephrotoxicity</li>
<li>Local: Pain and irritation at IM injection site.</li>
</ul>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Formulation:</p>

<li>Ampoule 2 ml containing 80 mg.</li>
</ul>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Dosage: IM (usual). I.V. adults 3 mg/kg q 8 hr up to 5 mg/kg daily.</p>
<ul>
<li>Children 2-2.5 mg/kg every 8 hr.</li>
<li>Newborns 2.5 mg/kg every 12 hr.</li>
<li>Ophthalmic solution 0.3%, 1-2 drops every 15-30 minutes.</li>
<li>Topical ointment 0.1%, 1-5 times daily to the affected area.</li>
<li>N.B.: should not be mixed with other drugs for parenteral use.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chloramphenicol">Chloramphenicol:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chloramphenicol" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>&gt; Trade names: chloromycetin, synthomycetin, synthomycin
&gt; N.B.: It can be extremely toxic due to protein synthesis inhibition in rapidly proliferating cells as bone marrow and should not be used for simple infections.
&gt; Available for hospital use only.
&gt; Action: it inhibits protein synthesis in bacteria by binding to ribosomes. The drug is mostly bacteriostatic — bactericidal in high doses, well absorbed from the GI tract and distributed to all parts of the body including C.S.F.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="e37468b1"><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Uses (indications):-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#e37468b1" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>○ NB: Not to be used for trivial infections as prophylaxis of infection, cold, throat infections or flu.
○ Treatment of choice for typhoid fever (not for carrier state).
○ Meningitis due to hemophilus influenza, pneumocoeoi or miningocoei.
○ Skin infections (topically).
○ Brain abscesses.
○ Eye and ear infections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="contraindications">Contraindications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>○ Hypersensitivity to chloramphenicol.
○ Pregnancy
○ Nursing mothers.</p>
<p>54</p>
<p>○ Renal and hepatic failure.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects">Side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>&gt; Aplastic anemia, pancytopnea, nausea, vomiting, abdominal distention, —progressive pallid cyanoses, ashen gray color, tachypnea, vasomotor collapse &amp; death, Gray syndrome in infants, super infections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="drug-interactions">Drug interactions:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-interactions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>○ Acetaminophen (acamol) increases the effect of chloramphenicol. (increases serum levels)
○ Oral anticoagulants: increases the effect of anticoagulant (decreases it's breakdown by the liver)</p>
<p>&gt; Formulation: tablets 250 mg, vial 1g.
&gt; Dosage: 50 mg/kg daily in 4 divided doses q 6hr (500 mg to 1 gm q 6 hr).
&gt; Drug considerations:</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>○ Administer I.V. as 10% solution over at least 1 min.
○ Note any history of hypersensitivity &amp; other contraindications, &amp; if client takes antidiabetic or other medications that cause bone marrow depression.
○ Neonates should be observed closely (greater hazards of toxicity).
○ Arrange for further hematologic studies to be conducted every 2 days to detect early signs of bone marrow depression.
○ The drug should be taken at regular intervals to be most effective.
○ The drug should be taken 1 hr before or 2 hr after meals (if GI upset occurs it can taken e food).</p>
<p>55</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="erythromycin">Erythromycin:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#erythromycin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>&gt; Action: Inhibits protein synthesis of microorganisms by binding to ribosome.
&gt; It is effective only against rapidly multiplying organisms.
&gt; Absorbed well from the upper GIT (small intestine).
&gt; Are manufactured in enteric –coated or film-coated forms to prevent destruction by gastric acid, diffuse poorly to C.S.F. &amp; primarily excreted in bile.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1cfcaed8"><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Uses:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1cfcaed8" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The drug of choice to treat respiratory tract infections.
Intestinal amebiasis.
An alternative drug to treat the following conditions in patients who are allergic to penicillin.</p>
<ul>
<li>Infections due to group A- beta hemolytic streptococci.</li>
<li>To prevent bacterial endocarditis prior to dental procedures.</li>
<li>Venereal disease (gonorrhea or syphilis).</li>
<li>Conjunctivitis of the newborn.</li>
<li>Long term prophylaxes in rheumatic fever.</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Contraindication: Hypersensitivity.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects">Side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>○ Nausea, vomiting, diarrhea, skin rashes, Hepatotoxicity, confusion.
I.V. uses: thrombophlebitis
○ Hearing loss: in patients receiving high doses or with renal</p>

<p>function impairment.</p>
<p>56</p>
<p>&gt; Formulation: Tablets 250 mg, suspension, 125 mg, 200 mg, 400 mg.</p>
<p>&gt; Dosage:</p>
<ul>
<li>The usual adult dose is 250 mg q 6 hr (can be doubled in severe infections).</li>
<li>Children, 30-50 mg/kg in divided doses.</li>

<ul>

<li>In the treatment of streptococcal infections, should be administered for at least 10 days.</li>
<li>Don't administer with fruit juice or other acidic drinks because it may decrease the activity of the drug.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="miscellaneous-antibiotics">Miscellaneous Antibiotics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#miscellaneous-antibiotics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-vancomycin-hydrochloride">1. Vancomycin Hydrochloride:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-vancomycin-hydrochloride" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>&gt; Trade name: vancocin.</p>
<p>&gt; Class: Antibiotic, miscellaneous.</p>
<p>&gt; Action: It appears to bind to bacterial cell wall, arresting it's synthesis and lysing the cytoplasmic membrane by a mechanism that is different from that of penicillin. It is bactericidal for most organisms and bactereostatic for enterococci.</p>
<p>&gt; N.B.: It is poorly absorbed from GIT so it should be administered parenterally only for life threatening infections.</p>
<p>&gt; Uses: drug should be reserved for treatment of life threatening infections when other treatment have been ineffective.</p>
<ul>
<li>Patients with severe staphylococcal infections resistant or allergic to penicillins or cephalosporinssch as:</li>
</ul>
<p>57</p>
<ul>
<li>Endocarditis * Osteomyelitis</li>
<li>Pneumonia * Septicemia</li>
<li>Oral administration is useful in treatment of:</li>
<li>enterocolitis * pseudomemgranous colitis</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Contraindications:</p>
<ul>
<li>Hypersensitivity * Minor infectious.</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Side effects:</p>
<ul>
<li>Ototoxicity deafness</li>
<li>Nephrotoxicity uremia</li>
<li>Red-Neck syndrome: —chills, erythema of neck and back fever|.</li>
<li>Skin rashes, Drug fever</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Hypotension (due to rapid administration).</li>
<li>Thrombophleptitis at site of injection.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Drug interactions:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Never give with other ototoxic or nephrotoxic agents especially aminoglycosides.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Dosage:</strong> Caps., syrup, or I.V. 0.5 g q 6 hr or 1 g q 12 hr.</p>
<p><strong>Drug considerations:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Mix as indicated on package insert.</li>
<li>Intermittent infusion is the preferred route.</li>
<li>Avoid rapid I.V. administration nausea &amp; hypotension.</li>
<li>Avoid extravasation during injections.</li>
<li>Monitor vital signs, intake of output, kidney function test.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>2. Ciprofloxacin Hydrochloride:</strong></p>
<p><strong>Trade name:</strong> cipro (ciproxin)</p>
<p><strong>Class.</strong> Antibacterial, quinolone derivative.</p>
<p>58</p>
<p><strong>Action:</strong> it has broad- spectrum bactericidal activity, inhibits the synthesis of bacterial DNA by inhibiting the enzyme DNA gyrase.</p>
<p><strong>Uses:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>UIT, infectious diarrhea</li>
<li>Infection of lower respiratory tract, bone, joints &amp; skin.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Contraindications:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Hypersensitivity - children - lactation.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Side-effects:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Nausea vomiting, dysphagia, crystalluria, hematuria.</li>
<li>Rashes, bad taste, GI bleeding, Headache, insomnia.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Dosage:</strong> 250-500 mg q 12 hr for 7-14 days.</p>
<p><strong>Drug considerations:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Give medication 2 hr after meals.</li>
<li>Stress importance of drinking increased amounts of fluids to keep urine acidic &amp; to minimize the risk of crystalluria.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Tetracyclines</strong></p>
<p><strong>Action:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>The tetracyclines inhibit protein synthesis of microorganisms by binding to its ribosomes, thereby interfering with protein synthesis.</li>
<li>The drugs are mostly bacteriostatic and are effective only against multiplying bacteria.</li>
<li>Well absorbed from the stomach &amp; upper GIT. And can pass through the placental barrier.</li>
<li>N.B.: They are deposited in the fetal skeleton and calcifying teeth.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects-most-common">Side effects: most common:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-most-common" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<ul>
<li>Don't use outdated or deteriorated drugs. Discard unused medications.</li>
<li>Administer I.M. deeply in large muscle mass.</li>
<li>Administer on an empty stomach (1 hr before or 2 hr after meals).</li>
<li>If the client is female &amp; pregnant, determine what trimester she is in.</li>
<li>Report side effects to physician.</li>
<li>Avoid direct sunlight, which can cause severe sunburn-like reaction.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sulfonamides">Sulfonamides<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sulfonamides" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Bacteria needs para-aminobenzoic acid dihydrofolic acid to multiply.</li>
<li><strong>Action:</strong> sulfonamides are structurally related to para-aminobenzoic</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
5
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>acid, the bacteria take it instead of these acids. So, tetrahydrofolic acid is not formed which is necessary for synthesis of DNA; therefore, there will be no cell multiplication.</p>
<ul>
<li>Bacteriostatic, not bactericidal.</li>
<li>Relatively inexpensive drugs.</li>
<li>Excreted mainly via kidneys.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Uses:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Less useful because of bacterial resistance &amp; development of other antibiotics.</li>
<li>UTI, e.g. E. coli, proteus &amp; staph. Aureus. —cephalosporines are given now.</li>
<li>To eliminate meningococci from nasopharynx (carriers).</li>
<li>As alternative to penicillin for prophylaxis from rheumatic fever.</li>
<li>As alternative to tetracycline in treatment of chlamydia, trachoma &amp; conjunctivitis.</li>
<li>In combination with penicillin to treat otitis media.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Contraindications:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Pregnancy except for treatment of toxoplasmosis.</li>
<li>Used with caution in patients with impaired liver &amp; kidney function &amp; blood disorders.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Side effects</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Nausea, vomiting, stomatitis, abdominal pain, headache, dizziness, ataxia, photosenitivity, rash.</li>
<li>Steven–Johnson syndrome (rhinitis, conjunctivitis, fever, stomatitis, &amp; rash).</li>
<li>Renal damage: crystalluria, hematuria, proteinuria.</li>
<li>Hemolytic anemia, aplastic anemia, Jaundice.</li>
<li>Super-infection.</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Note: Vitamin K should be administered to patient take long-term sulfonamide since, it kills normal flora.</p>
<p><strong>Nursing consideration:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Obtain a complete nursing and drug history.</li>
<li>If the client is pregnant, the physician should be informed so that, another type of medication not harmful to a developing fetus may be used.</li>
<li>During drug therapy, assess client for any of the following: reactions that may require withdrawal of the drugs:</li>
</ul>

<p><strong>Urinary Germicides\Analgesics</strong>
&gt; UTI may be treated with one of the sulfonamides, antibiotic or drugs discussed in this chapter.</p>
<p>1- Nalidixic Acid: negram, urogram (quinolone)
&gt; Class: urinary germicide.
&gt; Action: Inhibit DNA synthesis of the microorganism.
&gt; Partially metabolized in the liver &amp; rapidly execrated in urine.
&gt; Sensitivity determination is recommended.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-nitrofurantoin-furadantin">2- Nitrofurantoin: Furadantin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-nitrofurantoin-furadantin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; Class: urinary germicide
&gt; Action: Interfere with bacterial CHO metabolism. It also interferes with bacterial cell wall synthesis.</p>
<p>66</p>
<p>&gt; Bacteriostatic at low concentration, bactericidal at high concentration.
&gt; Uses: severe UTI (pyelonephritis, cystitis).
&gt; Contraindications: anuria, oliguria, impaired renal function. Pregnancy, lactation, infant less than 1 month of age.
&gt; Special concerns: used with caution in patients with anemia, DM, electrolyte imbalance, avitaminosis, debilitating disease.
&gt; Side effect: Nausea, vomiting, pancreatitis, abdominal pain, leukopenia, megaloblastic anemia, headache, vertigo, hemolytic anemia in patients with G-6-PD deficiency.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-norfloxacin-apirol-quinolone">4- Norfloxacin: Apirol (quinolone)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-norfloxacin-apirol-quinolone" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; Class: urinary germicide
&gt; Action: Against gram positive and gram negative organisms by inhibiting DNA synthesis. Not effective against obligate anaerobes.
&gt; Uses: complicated and uncomplicated UTI.
&gt; Contraindications: Hypersensitivity to negram, lactation, children.
&gt; Side effects: nausea, vomiting, heartburn, abdominal pain, leukopenia.
&gt; Dose: Tabs. 400 mg bid for 7-10 days.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-phenazopyridine-sedural">5- Phenazopyridine: sedural<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-phenazopyridine-sedural" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; Class: Urinary analgesic.
&gt; Action: Azo dye has local anesthetic effect on UTI.
&gt; Uses: pain relief in chronic UTI, irritation, trauma instrumentation. (Not For Treatment of UTI).</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="antifungal-agents">Antifungal Agents<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antifungal-agents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Several types of fungi or yeasts are pathogenic for humans.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Fungal infections may be systemic, limited to skin, hair or nails or infect moist mucous membranes including the GI tract and vagina.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Candida organisms belong to this group.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Drug therapy depends both on the infectious agent &amp; on the type of infection.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> An accurate diagnosis of the infection before therapy is most important for the choice of the therapeutic agents.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> It is important that drug therapy be continued until the infectious agent has been completely eradicated to avoid the emergence of resistant strains.</p>

<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Action: It is natural antifungal, antibiotic that is derived from streptomyces noursei &amp; both fungistatic &amp; fungicidal against all species of candida. It binds to fungal cell membranes —sterols], resulting in altered cellular membrane permeability &amp; leakage of potassium &amp; other essential components.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> It is excreted in feces.

<p><strong>Anthelmintics</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Helminths (worms) may infest the intestinal mucosa of lumen and can migrate to a particular tissue.</li>
<li>Treatment of worms' infection is complicated since a worm may have one or more morphological stages.</li>
<li>All family members should be examined since infestations are transmitted by sharing bathrooms (hygiene is very important).</li>
<li>Worms divided into 3 groups:</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>A. Cestodes:</strong>
Tape worm e.g. taenia saginata (beef), taenia solium (pork).</p>
<p><strong>B. Nematodes:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Filaria: filariasis</li>
<li>Hook worm: ancylostoma.</li>
<li>Pinworm: oxyuriasis (common in school age).</li>
<li>Round worm: ascaris (can cause GI &amp; respiratory obstruction).</li>
<li>Threadworm: strongoloid.</li>
<li>Whipworm.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>C. Trematodes: Bilharziasis</strong></p>
<p><strong>Nursing considerations:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Instruct responsible family member how to prevent infestation with pinworm by :</li>
<li>Washing hands after toiling + before meals.</li>
</ul>
<p>71</p>
<ul>
<li>Keep nails short.</li>
<li>Applying antipruritic ointment to anal area to reduce scratching which transfers pin worms.</li>
<li>Alert all family members to be examined for pinworms.</li>
<li>Emphasize the need for follow-up examinations to check the results of treatment.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>1- Mebendazole: vermox</strong></p>
<p><strong>Class:</strong> anthelmintic.</p>
<p><strong>Action:</strong> By blocking the glucose uptake of the organism which leads to worm death.</p>
<p><strong>Uses:</strong> whipworm, pinworm, roundworm.</p>

<p>Special concerns: Pregnancy, children less than 2 years.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-piperazine-vermizine">2- Piperazine: vermizine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-piperazine-vermizine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Class: anthelmintic</li>
<li>Action: Paralyze the muscle of the parasite, which leads to dislodge &amp; excretion of parasite.</li>
<li>Absorbed via GIT, metabolize in liver &amp; excreted in urine.</li>
<li>Uses: Pinworm (oxyuriasis), round worm (ascariasis).</li>
<li>Note: Recommended for pediatric use.</li>
</ul>
<p>72</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="amebicides-and-trichomonocides">Amebicides and trichomonocides<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#amebicides-and-trichomonocides" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-metronidazole-flagyl">1- Metronidazole: Flagyl<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-metronidazole-flagyl" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Class: systemic trichomonocide, amebicide.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Action:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Effective against anaerobic bacteria &amp; protozoa.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Inhibit growth of trichomona &amp; amebae by binding to DNA &amp; inhibit nucleic acid synthesis; resulting in cell death.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Well absorbed from GIT &amp; widely distributed in tissues.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Eliminated in urine (primarily), 20% unchanged, resulting in red, brown discoloration in urine following P.O. or I.V. use.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Uses:</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>A - Systemic:</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>1- Amebiasis, trichomoniasis.</th><th>2- Amebic dysentery.</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>3- Amebic liver abscess.</td><td>4- Septicemia</td></tr><tr><td>5- Endocarditis</td><td>6- Giardiosis</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>7- To control anaerobic infections of the abdomen following colorectal surgery, hystrectomy, emergency appendectomy.</p>
<p>B. Topical :</p>
<ol>
<li>Inflammatory papules &amp; pstules.</li>
</ol>

<ul>
<li>Active organic disease of CNS.</li>
<li>Blood disorders</li>
<li>Lactation.</li>
<li>1st trimester of pregnancy.</li>
<li>Topical Hypersensitivity.</li>
