<li>If used IV, drug should not be given by IV bolus.</li>
<li>If a primary IV fluid setup is used, discontinue the primary solution during infusion of metronidazole.</li>
<li>Report any symptoms of CNS toxicity immediately, e.g. ataxia or tremor, which necessitate withdrawal of drug.</li>
<li>The drug may turn urine brown.</li>
<li>Explain for the male partner, the necessity to have therapy.</li>
</ul>
<p>2- Povidone Iodine: Betadine</p>
<p>&gt; Class: Antiseptic, germicide.</p>
<p>&gt; Action: Is a non-stinging, non-staining iodine complex with all of the antiseptic properties of iodine but without skin &amp; mucus membrane irritation.</p>
<p>&gt; Bactericidal for gram positive &amp; negative bacteria, antibiotic resistant organisms, fungi, viruses, protozoa &amp; yeast.</p>
<p>&gt; Uses:</p>
<ul>
<li>Topical dressing - Antiseptic for wounds &amp; burns.</li>
</ul>
<p>74</p>
<ul>
<li>Degerming of skin - Preoperatively.</li>
<li>Treatment of dandruff.</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Contraindications: skin hypersensitivity.</p>
<p>&gt; Dose: on full strength (solution or ointment) only once.</p>
<p>Antiviral Drugs</p>
<p>&gt; Most antibiotics are ineffective against viruses.</p>
<p>&gt; Vaccines have been widely used to prevent certain viral infections e.g measles, small pox, polio ...</p>
<p>&gt; Treatment of AIDS.</p>
<p>1- Acyclovir : Zovirax</p>
<p>&gt; Class. : Antiviral, anti-infective</p>
<p>&gt; Action: Drug is converted to acyclovir triphosphate which interferes with herpes simplex virus DNA polymerase and</p>
<p>therefore, inhibit DNA replication.</p>
<p><strong>Uses:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>P.O.: for initial and recurrent herpes infection in immunocompromised &amp; nonimmunocompromised patients.</li>
<li>Parenteral: initial therapy of severe genital herpes, varicella zoster infection in immunocompromised patients.</li>
<li>Herpes simplex encephalitis.</li>
<li>Topical: it decreases duration of healing in limited nonlife threatening infection.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Contraindications:</strong> Hypersensitivity.</p>
<p><strong>Side effects:</strong>
P.O: nausea, vomiting, anorexia, sore throat.
Parenteral: phlebitis, hypotension, skin rash.</p>
<p>Topical: Burning pain.</p>
<p><strong>Dose:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Caps. &amp; tabs: Initial 200 mg /4 hrs for a total of 5 caps\day for 10 days.</li>
<li>Chronic: 200 mg t.i.d for up to 12 months.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>2- Amantadine; Symmetrel</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Class: Antiviral, antiparkinson</li>
<li>Action: Prevent penetration of the virus into cell, may be by preventing uncoating of RNA.</li>
<li>Uses: Influenza A viral infection.</li>
<li>Symptomatic treatment of idiopathic Parkinson.</li>
<li>Parkinsonism syndrome postencephalitis.</li>
<li>Contraindications: Hypersensitivity.</li>
<li>Side effects: Nausea, vomiting, constipation, anorexia, CHF, leukopenia.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Antineoplastic Agents</strong>
Treatment of tumors involves one or a combination of the following treatment modalities:</p>
<ol>
<li>Surgery</li>
<li>Radiation</li>
<li>Chemotherapy</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Chemotherapy:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Antineoplastic or cytotoxic (cell poisons) drugs: toxic and interfere with the growth of normal as well as abnormal cells specially rapidly growing cells; e.g bone marrow, GI mucosal epithelium &amp; hair follicles.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Side effects:</strong></p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Bone marrow depression: leukopnea, thrombocytoprea, anemia.</li>
<li>Hair follicles: alopicia.</li>
<li>GI: nausea, vomiting, stomatitis.</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; General nursing considerations for antineoplastic agents:</p>
<ul>
<li>Administration:</li>
<li>Should be prepared by trained personnel (not by a pregnant).</li>
<li>Prepared away from cooling or heating vents &amp; other people.</li>
<li>Use latex gloves to protect skin.</li>
<li>Wash hands before and after preparation.</li>
<li>Wear non-permeable surgical gown with a close front, fit knit cuffs.</li>
<li>Use piggyback setup with electronic infusion pump.</li>
<li>Start infusion with solution not containing vesicant agent.</li>
<li>If possible, not use dorsum of the hand, wrist &amp; antichubital fossa, as a site of infusion &amp; don’t previously used sites.</li>
<li>After starting unmedicated solution, check for blood return, pain, redness and edema.</li>
<li>Instruct client to report pain, redness, and edema during &amp; after treatment.</li>
<li>Intake and output monitoring.</li>
<li>Report any extravasation to physician &amp; follow policy to minimize effect.</li>
</ul>
<p>77</p>
<ul>
<li>Bone Marrow depression:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Leukopenia:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Check WBC count and sudden drop less than 2000/mm³.</li>
<li>Check temperature every 4 hours, report fever more than 38°C.</li>
<li>Assess skin and body orifices for signs of infections.</li>
<li>Prevent infection by meticulous body care and strict medical asepsis.</li>
<li>Provide mouth care every 4-6 hours.</li>
<li>Reverse isolation:</li>
<li>☑ Private room.</li>
<li>☑ Gloves, masks, gowns as ordered.</li>
<li>☑ Limit articles brought to room.</li>
<li>☑ Infected personnel (staff &amp; visitors) not to inter this room.</li>
<li>Change IV infusion every 24 hours, IV site every 48 hours.</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li>Compare client’s nutritional status and weight with baseline established at starting of therapy.</li>
<li>Determine if the client has anorexia.</li>
<li>Premedicating with antiemetic as ordered.</li>
<li>Administering antineoplastics on empty stomach to minimize nausea and vomiting.</li>
<li>Encourage ingestion of dry carbohydrates such as toast before therapy.</li>
<li>Consider likes and dislikes of the patient.</li>
<li>Encourage intake of high protein diet.</li>
<li>Provide good oral hygiene both before and after meals.</li>
<li>Provide supportive care to keep client comfortable and clean and free from odors.</li>
<li>Correction of electrolytes may be required.</li>

<p>A) Alkylating Agents:
&gt; Action: are highly reactive in that under physiologic conditions they donate an alkyl group to biologically important molecules as DNA.</p>
<ol>
<li>Carboplatin: paraplatin.
&gt; Class: antineoplastic, alkylating agent.
&gt; Uses: ovarian cancer.
&gt; Additional Side effects: neurotoxicity, nephrotoxicity.</li>
</ol>
<p>79</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Cyclophosphamide (CYC): cytoxan</li>
</ol>
<p>&gt; Class: antineoplastic, alkylating agent.
&gt; Uses: multiple myloma, malignant lymphomas, Hodgkin’s disease.
&gt; Additional Side effects: alopecia, bone marrow depression, hemolytic cystitis, darkening of skin &amp; fingernails.</p>
<p>Ifosfamide: Ifex</p>
<p>&gt; Class.: antineoplastic, alkylating agent.
&gt; Uses: acute leukemia, testicular cancer, malignant lymphomas.
&gt; Additional Side effects: hemorrhagic cystitis.</p>
<p>B) Antimetabolites:</p>
<p>&gt; Action: Disrupt DNA replication by interfering with an essential step in its synthesis and metabolism.</p>
<ol>
<li>Cytabine: cytosar</li>
</ol>
<p>&gt; Class: antineoplastic, antimetabolite.
&gt; Uses: acute myelocytic leukemia, Hodgkin’s lymphoma.
&gt; Additional Side effects: cytabine syndrome occurs 6-12 hours following administration manifested by myalgia, fever, and bone pain.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Methotrexate (MTX): abitexate</li>
</ol>
<p>&gt; Class.: antimeabolite, folic acid analog.
&gt; Action: similar to sulfonamide, it decreases purine and DNA synthesis.
&gt; Uses: uterine choriocarcinoma (cancer of the placenta), vesicular mole, leukemia.</p>
<ul>
<li>In low doses for treatment of rheumatoid arthritis. Action isn’t known.</li>
</ul>
<p>80</p>
<p>&gt; Side effects: severe bone marrow depression, hepatotoxicity, hemorrhagic enteritis, transient paresis or seizures.
&gt; Given intravenously and intrathecally.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="e-hormonal-and-antihormonal-antineoplastic-agents">E) Hormonal and antihormonal antineoplastic agents:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#e-hormonal-and-antihormonal-antineoplastic-agents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="iron-preparations">Iron Preparations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iron-preparations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A complex of iron and other substances are normally taken orally.</li>
<li>Sometimes administered parenterally when:</li>
<li>Some disorders limiting the amount of drug absorbed by GIT.</li>
<li>Patient is unable to tolerate oral iron.</li>
<li>Iron deficiency is common in infants (low iron in diet), and during pregnancy (increased requirements).</li>
<li><strong>Action</strong>: Iron (diet or drug) absorbed from GIT and transport to bone marrow after combining with protein transferrin, to incorporate with hemoglobin.</li>
<li><strong>Uses</strong>: prophylaxis and treatment of iron deficiency anemia.</li>
<li><strong>Contraindications</strong>: Hemosiderosis, peptic ulcer, enteritis, ulcerative colitis and liver cirrhosis.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="drug-interactions">Drug interactions:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-interactions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Antacids: decrease absorption of iron.</li>
<li>Tetracycline: iron diminishes affect of tetracycline (decrease its absorption).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Constipation, gastric irritation, and abdominal cramps, change color of stool to black.</li>
<li>Toxic reaction: (parenteral): causes nausea, vomiting, peripheral vascular collapse. Occurs within 60 seconds of toxic dose. Symptoms may disappear then reappear after 6-24 hours.</li>
</ul>
<p>83</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-iron-toxicity">Treatment of iron toxicity:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-iron-toxicity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptomatic treatment.</li>
<li>Induce vomiting, then give egg and milk.</li>
<li>Gastric lavage may be done with IV NaHCO₃ solution to counteract acidosis.</li>
<li>Give antidote (chelliating agent); IV infusion of deferoxamine (desferal).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Take a complete history, including use of antacids.</li>
<li>Ask about any evidence of GI bleeding.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>

<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Advise client to take iron with meals to reduce gastric irritation.
Take iron with citrus juices to enhance absorption.
Advise client not to take iron with milk, tea, or antacids (they decrease iron absorption).
Encourage client to eat a well balanced diet.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>◯</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\bigcirc</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">◯</span></span></span></span></span> Keep drug out of reach of children (extremely toxic).
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>◯</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\bigcirc</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">◯</span></span></span></span></span> When administering iron to child, dilute it with water or fruit juice &amp; use a straw to minimize teeth staining.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>◯</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\bigcirc</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">◯</span></span></span></span></span> Discuss with client the possibility of indigestion, changes in stool color (black) and constipation.</p>
<ol>
<li>Ferrus Sulfate: Ferrograd, Eryfer

<p>84</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>◯</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\bigcirc</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">◯</span></span></span></span></span> Prophylaxis: 300 mg daily.
Treatment: 300 mg bid.</p>

<li>Iron dextran injection: imferon
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Class.: Iron preparation, parenteral.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> The only iron preparation used parenterally

<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Side effects: Anaphylaxis, rashes, nausea, vomiting, diarrhea, hypotension, tachycardia, shock.

<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>◯</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\bigcirc</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">◯</span></span></span></span></span> IV: leads to phlebitis.</li>

<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Nursing considerations:</p>
<ul>
<li>Should never be mixed with other medications or added to parenteral nutrition.</li>
<li>Obtain vital signs to determine client’s response to therapy.</li>
<li>Give the drug IM deeply or IV slowly.</li>
<li>Prevent staining of skin by using a separate needle.</li>
<li>Be prepared to assist with treatment of iron intoxication.</li>
</ul>
<p>Folic acid
Generic Name: Folvite</p>
<p>Action</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Stimulates production of red and white blood cells and platelets in some megaloblastic anemias.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indications-and-dosages">Indications and dosages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications-and-dosages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Recommended dietary allowance</li>
</ul>
<p>85</p>
<ul>
<li>Megaloblastic anemia related to folic acid deficiency in nutritional deficiency, pregnancy, childhood, or infancy.</li>
<li>Folate deficiency</li>
</ul>
<p>Dose: 150 to 400 mcg, up to 1 mg/day</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications-and-precautions">Contraindications and precautions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications-and-precautions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Contraindicated in pernicious, aplastic, or normocytic anemia</li>
<li>Use cautiously in breastfeeding patients.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adverse-reactions">Adverse reactions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adverse-reactions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Altered sleep pattern, malaise, poor concentration, impaired judgment, hyperactivity, anorexia, nausea, flatulence, bitter taste, allergic reaction (including rash, pruritus, erythema), Bronchospasm.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing Considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Teach woman about importance of taking daily dose 3 months before pregnancy and in first trimester as it decreases fetal neural tube defects by 50%.</li>
<li>It is not effective in normocytic anemias</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="anticoagulants-hemostaties">Anticoagulants &amp; Hemostaties<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anticoagulants-hemostaties" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Prothrombin (thromboplastion) thrombin</li>
<li>Fibrinogen (thrombin) fibrin (insoluble protein).</li>
<li>Several factors participate in blood clotting manufactured by the liver as vitamin K. (Liver disease affect blood clotting)</li>
<li>Many diseases lead to defect of coagulation (hemophilia, C.V. diseases).</li>
</ul>
<p>86</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="anticoagulants">Anticoagulants:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anticoagulants" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Warfarin sodium: coumadin</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Class: anticoagulant.</li>
<li>Action: prevent the formation of factors II, VII, IX and X in the liver.</li>
<li>Uses:</li>
<li>Prophylaxis and treatment of deep venous thrombosis.</li>
<li>Thromboembolison - Thrombophlebitis.</li>
<li>Prophylaxis from myocardial infarction.</li>
<li>Contraindications:</li>
<li>Hemorrhagic tendencies</li>
</ul>

<li>Heparin:</li>
</ol>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span>  Class: anticoagulant

<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span>  Must be given parentally.

<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span>  Action: Potentiate the inhibitory action of antithrombin III on various coagulation factors.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span>  Inactivate thrombin and prevent the conversion of fibrinogen to fibrin.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span>  Uses:</p>
<p>To prevent extension of clots.
To prevent thrombi and emboli from recurring.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>◯</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\bigcirc</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">◯</span></span></span></span></span>  Prophylactic from thromboembolic diseases.
After some types of surgery (cardiac, orthopedic &amp; vascular).
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>◯</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\bigcirc</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">◯</span></span></span></span></span>  Prevent clotting during hemodialysis.
Treatment of DIC (disseminated intravascular coagulation)
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>◯</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\bigcirc</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">◯</span></span></span></span></span>  Coronary occlusion after MI.</p>

<p>&gt; Contraindications:</p>
<ul>
<li>Blood disorders with bleeding tendencies (hemophilia).</li>
<li>Suspected intracranial hemorrhage.</li>
<li>Open wounds.</li>
<li>During surgery of the eyes, brain and spinal cord.</li>
</ul>
<p>88</p>
<ul>
<li>Menstruation.</li>
<li>Abortion.</li>
<li>Any drugs or conditions affecting blood coagulation.</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Side effects: Hemorrhage.
&gt; Overdose: nose bleeding, hematouria, petechiae, tarry stool.
&gt; Antidote: protamin sulfate.
&gt; Dose: IV or S.C measured in units according to bleeding &amp; clotting time.</p>
<p>&gt; Nursing considerations:</p>
<ul>
<li>Should not be administered IM, administer by deep sc to minimize local irritation and to prolong the action of drug.</li>
<li>Don't massage before and after injection.</li>
<li>Change site of administration to avoid ecchymosis.</li>
<li>Instruct and stress the importance of reporting any signs of active bleeding.</li>
<li>Use electric razor for shaving, soft bristle tooth brush to decrease gum irritation.</li>
<li>Patient should be hospitalized for IV therapy.</li>
<li>Clotting time, PTT should be done before the start of therapy each dose of drug then daily.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Enoxaparin sodium</li>
</ol>
<p>Trade name: Clexane, Lovenox 3</p>
<p>Class: Anticoagulant, low-molecular-weight heparin.</p>
<p>&gt; Pregnancy risk category B</p>
<p>Action
&gt; Inhibits thrombus and clot formation by blocking factor Xa and factor IIa. This inhibition accelerates formation of antithrombin</p>
<p>89</p>
<p>III-thrombin complex (a coagulation inhibitor), thereby deactivating thrombin and preventing conversion of fibrinogen to fibrin.</p>
<p>Indications and dosages
&gt; Patients at risk for thromboembolic complications (pulmonary</p>
<p>embolism and deep-vein thrombosis) due to severely restricted mobility during acute illness or post a major surgery.</p>
<ul>
<li>Prevent blood clots.</li>
<li>In some cases of pregnancy (sometime, a blood clot is formed in the umbilical cord due to antiphospholid syndrome, which leads to miscourage).</li>
<li>Adults: 40 mg subcutaneously daily</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications">Contraindications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypersensitivity to clexane or heparin.</li>
<li>Thrombocytopenia</li>
<li>Active major bleeding</li>
<li>Major blood disorders</li>
<li>Certain types of stroke</li>
<li>Do not give Clexane to a child.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="precautions">Precautions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#precautions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Use cautiously in:</p>
<ul>
<li>Severe hepatic or renal disease, retinopathy (hypertensive or diabetic), uncontrolled hypertension, hemorrhagic stroke, bacterial endocarditis, GI bleeding or other bleeding disorders</li>
<li>Recent history of ulcer disease</li>
<li>Pregnant or breastfeeding patients</li>
<li>Children.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adverse-reactions">Adverse reactions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adverse-reactions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>CNS: dizziness, headache, insomnia, confusion, cerebrovascular accident</li>
<li>CV: edema, chest pain, atrial fibrillation, heart failure</li>
<li>GI: nausea, vomiting, constipation</li>
<li>GU: urinary retention</li>
<li>Hematologic: anemia, bleeding tendency, thrombocytopenia, hemorrhage</li>
<li>Skin: bruising, pruritus, rash, urticaria, irritation, or erythema at injection site</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Monitor CBC and platelet counts. Watch for signs and symptoms of bleeding or bruising.</li>
<li>Instruct patient to promptly report irregular heartbeat, unusual bleeding or bruising, rash.</li>
<li>Teach patient safety measures to avoid bruising or bleeding.</li>
</ul>

<p>Contraindications and precautions
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Contraindicated in hypersensitivity to drug

<p>Adverse reactions
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Hyperbilirubinemia (in infants); with parenteral administration—pain, swelling,
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> tenderness at injection site; itchy rash after repeated injections; transient flushing sensations; anaphylic reaction.</p>
<p>Thrombolytic Agents</p>
<ul>
<li>Agents used to promote the dissolution (lysis) of the insoluble fibrin trapped in intravascular emboli and thrombi.</li>
<li>The most serious complication is hemorrhage.</li>
<li>Heparin therapy usually follows treatment with these agents.</li>
</ul>
<p>1- Streptokinase:
Class: Thrombolytic agent.
Action: Acts with plasminogen to produce an activator complex which enhance the conversion of plasminogen to plasmin which breaks down fibrinogen, fibrin clot &amp; other plasma proteins.
Uses: Deep venous thrombosis (DVT)
Myocardial infarction (MI)
To clear occluded arteriovenous or IV canula.
Contraindication: Hemorrhage.
Side effects: Bleeding, nausea, and headache.</p>
<p>92</p>
<p>Antifibrinolytic agents
Tranexamic acid
Trade Name: Hexacaprone
Classification: Antifibrinolytic
Uses: Prevention of heavy bleeding such as heavy periods, nose bleeds
Prevention of bleeding during tooth extraction in haemophiliacs (people who</p>
<p>This document is available on
5
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>lack a clotting factor)</p>
<p>Contraindications: pregnancy, breast feeding, history of thromboembolic disease, kidney problems, bleeding disorders, and menstrual bleeding.</p>
<p>Side-effects: Nausea, vomiting, Diarrhea</p>
<p>Nursing considerations:</p>
<ol>
<li>To overcome GI problems, instruct patient to eat little and often, and eat simple foods such as dry toast.</li>
<li>Teach patient to drink plenty of fluids.</li>
<li>Watch for thrombus or embolus formation</li>
<li>Teach patient to report sudden slurred speech, loss of co-ordination, pain in the chest or groin or leg you should contact a doctor as soon as possible. If any of these occur, stop taking the medication and see your doctor.</li>
</ol>
<p>93</p>
<p>Cardiac drugs</p>
<p>Cardiac glycosides</p>
<ul>
<li>Digitoxins are plant alkaloids.</li>
<li>They increase myocardial contractions, which will increase blood supply to all organs including the kidneys therefore causing diuresis, which will decrease the edema.</li>
<li>They are used to treat cardiac arrhythmia because they decrease heart rate.</li>
</ul>
<p>Action:</p>
<ul>
<li>They increase the force of myocardial contractions (positive inotropic).</li>
<li>They increase the contractility of the heart muscle by minimizing the movement of Na and K ions and increasing the release of Ca ions in the myocardial cells.</li>
<li>It decreases the heart rate due to increase in parasympathetic nervous system and decrease in the sympathetic tone.</li>
<li>They are primarily excreted through the kidneys.</li>
<li>The initial dose is the larger dose (the loading or digitalizing dose), the subsequent doses are referred to as (Maintenance doses).</li>
</ul>
<p>Results:</p>
<ul>
<li>Decrease in venous pressure.</li>
<li>Coronary dilatation.</li>
<li>Reduce heart size.</li>
<li>Marked diuresis and decreasing edema.</li>
</ul>
<p>Indications:</p>
<ol>
<li>Congestive heart failure (C.H.F).</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>94</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Cardiac arrhythmia (atrial fibrillation, atrial flutter and sinus tachycardia).</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Contraindication:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Hypersensitivity.</li>
<li>Angina pectoris in absence of CHF.</li>
<li>Given with caution for elderly and people who have kidney failure.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Side effects:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>They are extremely toxic and may cause death.</li>
<li>There is a narrow margin of safety between the therapeutic dose and the toxic dose.</li>
<li>Could cause overdose by cumulative effects of the drug so frequent assessment of the serum level is essential.</li>
<li>May cause cardiac arrhythmia such as bradycardia (below than 60 beat/minute) and other dysarrhythmia.</li>
<li>Nausea, vomiting, and diarrhea.</li>
<li>Headache, malaise and muscle weakness.</li>
<li>Skin rashes, blurring of vision, diplopia and while halos.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Patients suffering from digitalis intoxication should be admitted to the ICU for continuous monitoring of ECG. Administration of digitalis should be halted.</li>
<li>If serum potassium is below normal, administer K salts and give antiarrhythmic drugs as Lidocain as ordered by Dr.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Drug interactions:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Antacid (they decrease the effect of digitalis).</li>
<li>Fursemide (Lasix): it increase K loss and increase the chance for digitalis toxicity.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Predisposing factors for digitalis toxicity:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>K loss (hypokalemia) which results from: diuretics, NPO, gastric suction, and poor K intake.</li>
<li>Pathological conditions;
A) Liver disease: they decrease metabolism and therefore increase digitalis level.
B) Kidney disease: they decrease the excretion of drug and therefore increase digitalis levels.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Nursing considerations:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Check doctor’s order, medication record and bottle label accurately.</li>
<li>Observe monitor for evidence of bradycardia or arrhythmia.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
5 studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Measure intake and output accurately.</li>
<li>Weigh the patient in daily basis.</li>
<li>Pulse should be checked by 2 nurses.</li>
<li>Provide the client with foods high in potassium as banana, orange.</li>
<li>Monitor serum digoxin level.</li>
<li>Elderly people should be assessed for early signs of toxicity.</li>
<li>Have digoxin antidote available (digoxin immune FAB).</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Drugs:</strong></p>
<p><strong>Digoxin:</strong> Lanoxin</p>
<p><strong>Class:</strong> cardiac glycoside.</p>
<p>It is the drug of choice for CHF because of:</p>
<ol>
<li>It has rapid onset.</li>
<li>It has short duration.</li>
<li>It can be administered P.O. or IV.</li>
</ol>
<p>96</p>
<p><strong>Dose:</strong> digitalization dose = 0.4 – 0.6 mg followed by 0.05 – 0.35 mg once or twice daily.</p>
<p><strong>Antidote:</strong> Digoxin Immune FAB (Ovine)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="coronary-vasodilators">Coronary vasodilators<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#coronary-vasodilators" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-antianginal-drugs">1. Antianginal drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-antianginal-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><strong>Angina pectoris:</strong> is a clinical syndrome characterized by paroxysm of pain in the anterior chest caused by insufficient coronary blood flow and/or inadequate oxygen supply to the myocardial muscle.</p>
<p><strong>Causes:</strong> (1) Atherosclerosis. (2) Vasospasim.</p>
<p>There are three groups of drugs used for treatment of angina:</p>
<ol>
<li>Nitrates/nitrites.</li>
<li>Beta-adrenergic blocking agents.</li>
<li>Calcium channel blocking agents.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Nitrates/nitrites:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Nitrates/nitrites - Action: direct relaxation of blood vessels and smooth muscles vasodialtion O2 requirements.</li>
<li>relaxation of smooth muscles of coronary arteries coronary vasodialtion blood supply to the myocardium.</li>
<li>relaxation of arteries and veins BP workload in the heart.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Indications:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Prophylaxis and treatment of acute angina pectoris.</li>
<li>Treatment of chronic angina pectoris.</li>

<p>♦ Calcium channel blocking agents:</p>
<ul>
<li>Action: for contraction of cardiac and smooth muscle to occur, extracellular calcium must move into the cell through openings called calcium channels. These agents inhibit the influx of calcium through the cell membrane resulting in a depression of automatically and conduction velocity in both smooth and cardiac muscles leading to:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Myocardial contractility.</li>
<li>Inhibit spasm of coronary arteries dilatation.</li>
<li>Peripheral vasodilation peripheral resistance.</li>
<li>S. A. node automatically and conduction heart rate.</li>
</ol>

<p>▪ Nifedipine: Adalat</p>
<ul>
<li>Class: calcium channel blocking agent (anti-angina, antihypertensive).</li>
<li>Uses: vasospastic angina, essential hypertension.</li>
<li>Contraindications: hypersensitivity, lactation.</li>
<li>Side effects: pulmonary and peripheral edema, MI, hypotension, headache, muscle cramps, flushing.</li>
<li>Dosage: 10-30 mg tid.</li>
<li>In hypertensive emergencies: 10-20 mg given orally or sublingually by puncturing the capsule and squeezing contents under the tongue.</li>
</ul>
<p>▪ Verapamil: Ikacor</p>
<ul>
<li>Class: calcium channel blocking agent (anti-angina, antihypertensive).</li>
<li>Uses:</li>
<li>P.O: angina pectoris, arrhythmia (atrial fibrillation, and flutter).</li>
<li>Essential hypertension.</li>
<li>IV: supraventricular tachycardia.</li>
<li>Contraindications: hypotension, cardiac shock, and MI.</li>
<li>Side effects: AV block, bradycardia, headache, dizziness, abdominal cramps, blurring of vision, and edema.</li>
<li>Dosage: Initial 80-120 mg tid then 240-480 mg /day.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="antihypertensive-drugs">Antihypertensive drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antihypertensive-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>♦ Hypertension: is a condition in which the mean arterial blood pressure is elevated.
♦ Essential hypertension: could be mild, moderate, or severe and may lead to dangerous changes in kidneys, eyes and blood vessels.
♦ Secondary hypertension: a certain disease or condition leads to elevation of blood pressure such as toxemia or pregnancy, acute kidney failure, etc.
♦ Antihypertensive agents: are initiated when diastolic blood pressure is higher than 90mm/Hg.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-hypertension-includes">Treatment of hypertension includes:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-hypertension-includes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>weight reduction.</li>
<li>Sodium restriction.</li>
<li>Alcohol restriction.</li>
<li>Stop smoking.</li>
<li>Exercise.</li>
<li>Behavior modification.</li>
</ol>
<p>♦ Single drug should be considered from the following classes:</p>
<ol>
<li>Diuretics.</li>
<li>Beta-blocking agents.</li>
<li>Calcium channel blocking agents.</li>
<li>Angiotensin converting enzyme inhibitors.</li>
</ol>
<p>♦ Initial therapy is continued for one month. If there is no response, combination therapy is needed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>Determine base line blood pressure before starting antihypertensive treatment.
101</li>

<li>Ascertain lifestyle changes.</li>
<li>Determine client’s ability to take his BP measurement.</li>
<li>Record significant changes in BP readings.</li>
<li>Advise client to adhere to low sodium diet.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-angiotensin-converting-enzyme-inhibitors">1. Angiotensin-converting enzyme inhibitors:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-angiotensin-converting-enzyme-inhibitors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>♦ Captopril:</p>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Trade name: Capotin, nhabace.</li>
<li>Class: antihypertensive, inhibitor of angiotensin synthesis.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Action:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>captopril is a highly specific competitive inhibitor of angiotensin I converting enzyme. The enzyme is responsible for the conversion of angiotensin I to angiotensin II which decrease BP.</li>
<li>reduce peripheral arterial resistance.</li>
<li>Decrease aldosterone secretion which works to increase level of serum potassium.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Indications:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Hypertension.</li>
<li>In combination with diuretics and digitalis in the treatment of CHF.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Contraindication:</strong> Hypersensitivity, renovascular disease and pregnancy.</p>
<p><strong>Side effects:</strong> Skin rash, loss of taste, neutropnea, nausea, vomiting, hypotension, proteinuria, renal failure and hyperkalemia. 102</p>
<p><strong>Dosage:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Tablets: - 12.5 mg 2-3 time per day.</li>
<li>If there is no response, after 1-2 weeks, increase dose to 25 mg 2-3 time per day.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Nursing considerations:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>In case of overdose, give normal saline to restore BP.</li>
<li>Should not be discontinued without Dr. order.</li>
<li>Obtain baseline hematological studies, liver &amp; renal functions tests prior to beginning the treatment.</li>
<li>Determine client’s understanding of the therapy and if he/she takes other medications.</li>
<li>Observe client closely for hypotension 3 hours after the initial dose.</li>
<li>In case of hypotension, place client in supine position and give IV saline infusion.</li>
<li>Withhold potassium sparing diuretics and consult with physician (hyperkalemia may occur).</li>
<li>Take captopril 1 hour before meal or on an empty stomach.</li>
<li>Report skin rash, heartburn, and chest pain to physician.</li>
<li>Explain to client that he may develop loss of taste for 2-3 months, if it persist, notify the physician.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>2. Beta-adrenergic blocking agents:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Action: it combines with beta-adrenergic receptors to block the response to sympathetic nerve impulses, circulating catecholamines or adrenergic</li>

<p>drugs.</p>
<ul>
<li>β-adrenergic receptors have been classified as beta 1 (in the cardiac muscle) and beta 2 (in the bronchi and blood vessels).</li>

<p>103</p>
<ul>
<li>Blocking of β1 receptors HR, myocardial contractility and cardiac output BP.</li>
<li>Blocking of β2 receptors airway resistance (bronchospasm), and vasoconstriction.</li>

<p><strong>Methyldopa:</strong></p>
<p><strong>-Trade name:</strong> (Aldomin)</p>
<p><strong>-Classification:</strong> Antihypertensive, centrally acting antiadrenergic agent.</p>
<p><strong>-Action:</strong> The active metabolite alphamethylenorepinephrin lowers BP by stimulating central inhibitory alpha-adrenergic receptors.</p>
<p><strong>-Uses:</strong>- Hypertension &amp; hypertension crises (parenteral).</p>
<p><strong>-Contraindications:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Hypersensitivity,</li>
<li>Active hepatic diseases.</li>
<li>Pheochromocytoma.</li>

<p>Drugs affecting The Central Nervous system</p>
<p>Barbiturates:</p>
<ul>
<li>Phenobarbital :
Trade name: Luminal.
Class: sedative- anticonvulsant- barbiturate.</li>
</ul>
<p>Action:</p>
<ul>
<li>Long-acting barbiturate- act as a sedative- hypnotic and anticonvulsant by producing CNS depression.</li>
<li>It increases the inhibitory activity on nerve synapses.</li>
</ul>
<p>Uses:
1- Preanasthetic medication.
2- Sedation 3- Hypnotic 4- Epilepsy
5. in tetanus &amp; eclampsia ( as anticonvulsant) .
N.B.: should be given parenterally for anticonvulsant effect.</p>
<p>Contraindication: Hypersensitivity.
Side effects: Headache, fever, megaloblastic anemia, dizziness, hypotension, nausea, vomiting epigastric pain.
108</p>
<p>Forms and Dose:
Tablets 100mg, ampules 130mg in 1 cc
Sedation: 30-120 mg daily in 2-3 divided doses.
For adults: Hypnotic 100-320 mg at bed-time.
Anticonvulsant: I.V. 100-320 mg, repeated as necessary.
Preoperative sedation: I.M. only 130-200 mg – 60-90 minutes before surgery.
N.B: Luminal can be used in neonates as antihyper- bilirubinemia.</p>
<p>Over dose:
Manifested by tachycardia , hypothermia, coma, respiratory depression , absent reflexes, respiratory muscle relaxation, and vascular collapse.</p>
<p>Treatment of overdose toxicity:
1- Maintain &amp; assist respiration as indicated.
2- Support circulation by vasopressor &amp; I.V. fluids as required.
3- Aspirate stomach contents, take care to avoid pulmonary aspiration.
4- Diuretics may be given as ordered.
5- Intake &amp; output measurement.
6- Dialysis if indicated.</p>
<p>Nursing considerations:
1- If given I.V, closely monitor the rate of flow. Rapid administration may lead to respiratory depression.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>2- Monitor the site of I.V. for soft of extravasation which causes severe pain, nerve damage &amp; necrosis.
3- Avoid the use of alcoholic beverages.
4- Instruct the client not to drive a car or operate other hazardous machinery after taking the medication.</p>
<p>109</p>
<p>5- Take the medication only as prescribed.
6- If used for hypnotic effect, give <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mfrac><mn>1</mn><mn>2</mn></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\frac{1}{2}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.1901em; vertical-align: -0.345em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8451em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.345em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span> hr before bedtime.

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Shouldn't be used to treat nausea &amp; vomiting in children less than 6 months of age.</li>
<li>Should avoid getting solution on hands or clothing (it will cause dermatitis).</li>
<li>Solutions with marked discoloration should be discarded.</li>
<li>Note any history of seizures.</li>
</ul>
<p>112</p>
<ul>
<li>Take liver &amp; kidney function test periodically.</li>
<li>Document &amp; rotate injection sites.</li>
<li>Report side effects immediately.</li>
<li>Determine age of male patients &amp; assess for prostatic hypertrophy.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lithium-carbonate">Lithium carbonate:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lithium-carbonate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Trade name:</strong> lithium.</p>
<p><strong>Class:</strong> antipsychotic, antimanic.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="action">Action:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Action is not known. Theories trying to explain the action of this drug include effectiveness to an alteration in Na ion metabolism within nerve &amp; muscle cells — +K ion &amp; ATP aseβ in catecholamine neurotransmitter levels hyperactivity.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Control of manic and hypomanic episodes in manic depression patients.</li>
<li>Prophylactic of bipolar depression.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Dose:</strong> P.O. 600 mg tid or qid.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Drowsiness, dizziness, hand tremors, lethargy. Hypothyroidism, ECG changes, anorexia, dry mouth, nausea, vomiting, polyuria, leukocytosis slurred speech.</p>
<p>In case of toxication (blood level over 2.0 mmol/L): hyper-reflexia and hyperextension of limbs, convulsions, toxic psychosis, syncope, oliguria, circulatory failure, and coma.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications">Contraindications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Cardiovascular, renal diseases.</li>
<li>Brain damage.</li>
</ul>
<p>113</p>
<ul>
<li>Pregnancy &amp; lactation.</li>
<li>Dehydration.</li>
<li>Patients receiving diuretics.</li>
<li>Sodium depletion.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Nursing considerations:</p>
<ul>
<li>Monitor serum level of lithium every 1-2 weeks to prevent toxicity (normal level is 0.4 - 1.0 mmol/L and toxic level is above 1.5 mmol/L).</li>
<li>Monitor for pulse irregularities &amp; changes in B.P.</li>
<li>Provide diet adequate in sodium.</li>
<li>Monitor for signs &amp; symptoms of toxicity.</li>
<li>Avoid factors that enhance toxicity: dehydration, renal failure, infection, co-administration of diuretics, and sodium depletion (may occur with diuretics).</li>
<li>Maintain adequate fluid and sodium levels.</li>
<li>Withdrawal (stopping) drug should be gradual (over weeks)</li>
</ul>

Class.: antidepressant, tricyclic.
Action: prevent the presynaptic re-uptake of the neurotransmitters (norepinephrine and serotonine) which will increase their concentration at the synaptic area alleviate depression.
Dose: P.O. 75-150 mg /day in 1-3 divided doses.</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="phenytoin">Phenytoin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#phenytoin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<p>Class: anticonvulsant, antiarrhythmic.</p>
<p>Action: acts in the motor cortex of the brain to reduce the spread of electrical discharges from the rapidly firing epileptic foci in this area. Also activity of centers in the brain stem responsible for the tonic phase of grand mal seizures.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications">Contraindications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dose-for-arrhythmias">Dose for arrhythmias:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dose-for-arrhythmias" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing Considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1- I.V. phenytoin may forms a precipitate, so flush tubing by saline (not dextrose) before &amp; after administration.
2- Assess for hypersensitivity.
3- If a pregnant woman takes this drug, tell her not to breast-feed her baby.
4- Obtain liver &amp; kidney function studies.
5- Monitor serum drug levels on a routine basis.
6- During I.V. therapy, monitor B.P. for signs of hypotension.</p>
<p>116</p>
<p>7- Take e food to minimize GI upset.
8- If the patient is diabetic, monitor for signs of hypoglycemia.
9- Oral hygiene to minimize bleeding from the gum.
10- Report any excessive growth of hair.</p>

<ol start="2">
<li>Magnesium sulfate</li>
</ol>
<p>Class: Anticonvulsant, electrolyte, saline laxative.</p>
<p>Action:</p>
<ul>
<li>It is an important cation present in the extrcellular fluid.</li>
<li>It is an essential electrolyte for muscle contraction, certain enzyme system &amp; never transmissions.</li>
<li>Magnesium depresses CNS &amp; control convulsion by blocking the release of acetylcholine at the myoneural junction.</li>
</ul>
<p>Uses:</p>
<ul>
<li>Seizures associated with toxemia of pregnancy.</li>
<li>Epilepsy</li>
<li>laxative</li>
<li>Hypomagnesemia</li>
<li>In total parenteral nutrition</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications">Contraindications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<p>N.B.: Suppression of knee-Jerk reflex can be used to determine toxicity. Respiratory failure may result if drug is given after disappearance of this reflex.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-magnesium-intoxication">Treatment of Magnesium intoxication:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-magnesium-intoxication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

Have calcium glutinate readily available for I.V. use.  |
| --- | --- |
|  Dose : anticonvulsant | I.M. 1-5 g of 25% - 50% solution.  |</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>For I.V. administer: only 1.5 ml of 10% solution/minute.</li>
<li>For I.M., inject the drug deep into the muscle using 50% solution.</li>
<li>As a laxative, dissolve in a glass of ice water or other fluid to lessen disagreeable taste.</li>
<li>Obtain baseline Mg level.</li>
<li>Obtain history of kidney disease.</li>
<li>Check with the physician before administering magnesium if any of the following conditions exist:</li>
</ul>
<table><thead><tr><th>1-</th><th>Absent patellar or knee jerk reflex.</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>2-</td><td>R.R. less than 16\m</td></tr><tr><td>3-</td><td>Urinary output less than 100 ml\4 hrs.</td></tr><tr><td>4-</td><td>Patient has a history of heart block or myocardial damage.</td></tr></tbody></table>

<li>Have available I.V. calcium gluconate.</li>
<li>Don't administer drug 2 hrs preceding delivery of the baby.</li>

</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="narcotic-analgesics-antagonists">Narcotic Analgesics &amp; Antagonists<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#narcotic-analgesics-antagonists" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="narcotic-analgesics">Narcotic Analgesics:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#narcotic-analgesics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>It include opium such as morphine, codeine &amp; opium derivatives such as Meperidine.</li>
<li>These substances have similar pharmacological properties.</li>
<li>Meperidine (Demerol) is the best known.</li>
<li>The relative activity of all narcotic analgesics is measured against morphine.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="dependence-tolerance">Dependence &amp; Tolerance:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dependence-tolerance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Remember that all drugs of this group may lead to addiction.</li>
<li>Psychological &amp; physical dependence &amp; tolerance develop even when using in clinical doses.</li>
<li>Tolerance usually develops because the patient requires shorter periods of time between doses or larger doses for relief of pain.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Effects of narcotic analgesics:</strong></p>
<table><thead><tr><th>1-</th><th>On CNS:</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>- Alteration of pain perception (analgesia)</td><td>- Euphoria</td></tr><tr><td>- Drowsiness</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>-Mental clouding</td><td>- Change in mood</td></tr></tbody></table>
