<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="acute-toxicity">Acute toxicity:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acute-toxicity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Characterized by respiratory depression, deep sleep, stupor, coma, pinpoint pupil, R.R 2-4\m, cyanosis, hypotension, decreased urinary output, decreased temperature, clammy skin, and finally Death (due to Respiratory failure).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-acute-overdose">Treatment of acute overdose:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-acute-overdose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1- Induce vomiting or gastric lavage.
2- Artificial respiration.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>3- Give narcotic antagonist (Narcan).</p>
<p>N.B.:
Respiratory stimulants (caffeine) should not be used to treat depression from overdose of narcotics.</p>
<p>Chronic toxicity:</p>
<ul>
<li>The problem of chronic dependence on narcotics is well Know &amp; is not only the problem of the street but is also found often among those who have easy access to narcotics —physicians, nurses... Pharmacists||. Narcotic analgesics sometimes used for nontherapeutic purposes.</li>
<li>Signs &amp; symptoms:</li>
<li>Constricted pupil, constipation, skin infections, needle scar abscesses &amp; itching on the anterior surface of the body.</li>
<li>Withdrawal signs appear when drugs is withheld for 4-12 hrs. &amp; characterized by intense craving for the drug, insomnia, yawning, sneezing, vomiting, diarrhea, tremors, sweating, mental depression, muscular aches, pain, chills &amp; anxiety. (they are rarely life-threatening).</li>
</ul>
<p>Action of narcotic analgesics:</p>
<ul>
<li>Narcotic analgesics attach to specific receptor in the CNS resulting in analgesia- action</li>
</ul>
<p>121</p>
<ul>
<li>Action exactly is unknown but may be by decreasing cell membrane permeability to sodium transmission of pain impulses.</li>
</ul>
<p>Uses:</p>
<ul>
<li>Sever pain</li>
<li>Hepatic &amp; renal colic.</li>
<li>Preanesthetic medication</li>
<li>Postsurgical pain.</li>
<li>Diarrhea &amp; dysentry</li>
<li>Pain from MI, carcinoma.</li>
<li>Postpartum pain &amp; burns.</li>
<li>Antitussive.</li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindications:</p>
<ul>
<li>Asthmatic conditions</li>
<li>Emphysema</li>
<li>Sever obesity</li>
<li>Convulsions</li>
<li>Diabetic acidosis</li>
<li>Myxedema</li>
<li>Addisson's disease</li>
<li>Hepatic cirrhosis</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Respiratory depression, apnea, dizziness, euphoria, headache, mental clouding, insomnia, nausea, vomiting, constipation, dry mouth, skin rashes, laryngospasm, urinary retention, and decreased libido.</p>
<p>122</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Use supportive nursing measures as relaxation techniques to relieve pain before using nacrotics.</li>
<li>Explore the source of pain, use non-narcotic analgesia if possible.</li>
<li>Administer the medication when needed, prolonging the medication administration will decrease the effect of the medication.</li>
<li>Monitor vital signs &amp; mental status.</li>
<li>Monitor Respiratory rate (drug may lead to respiratory depression).</li>
<li>Monitor blood pressure (hypotension may occur)</li>
<li>Monitor pulse rate (if 60\m withhold the drug).</li>
<li>Watch for constricted pupils. Document it and notify the physician.</li>
<li>Monitor bowel function, since drug may cause constipation.</li>
<li>Encourage client to empty bladder every 3-4 hrs (since drug may cause urinary retention).</li>
<li>If client is bed ridden, use side rails.</li>
<li>Inform the client\family that the drug may become habit forming and leading to addiction.</li>
<li>Document any history of asthma or other contraindications.</li>
<li>Have emergency equipment and narcotic antagonist available.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-codeine-sulfate">1. Codeine sulfate:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-codeine-sulfate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Class.: Narcotic analgesic, morphine type.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="action">Action:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Resembles morphine pharmacologically but produce less effect on respiratory system, less nausea &amp; less vomiting.</li>
</ul>
<p>123</p>
<ul>
<li>In high doses (more than 60 mg), it will irritate the cough center, but in lower doses, it is a potent antitussive and is an ingredient in many cough syrups.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Relief of mild to moderate pain.</li>
<li>Antitussive.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dose">Dose:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Analgesic: 15-60 mg q 4-6 hrs.</li>
<li>Antitussive: 10-20 mg q 4-6 hrs.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Meperidine Hydrochloride “Pethedine Hydrochloride”:</li>
</ol>
<p>Trade name: Demerol</p>
<p>Class.: Narcotic analgesic, synthetic.</p>
<p>Action: Similar to opiates.</p>
<ul>
<li>It has no antitussive effect.</li>
<li>The duration of action is less than that of opium.</li>
</ul>
<p>Uses:</p>
<ul>
<li>Sever pain.</li>
<li>Renal &amp; hepatic colic.</li>
<li>Obstetric preanasthetic medication.</li>
<li>In minor surgeries.</li>
<li>Spasm of GI tract, uterus.</li>
<li>Prior to some diagnostic procedures e.g. cystoscope.</li>
<li>Post operative pain.</li>
</ul>
<p>Add. Contraindications:</p>
<ul>
<li>Hypersensitivity. - Convulsive states.</li>
<li>Children less than 6 months. - Head injuries.</li>
</ul>
<p>124</p>
<ul>
<li>Diabetic acidosis.</li>
</ul>
<p>Add. Side effects: Transient hallucinations, hypotension.</p>
<p>Dose:</p>
<p>Drug can is available in the form of tablets, syrup, I.M, S.C.</p>
<p>Dose is 50-100 mg Q 3-4 hr.</p>
<p>It can be given as I.V. continuous infusion on a concentration of 1 mg/ml.</p>
<p>It also can be given IV slowly, and should be diluted in a concentration of 10mg/ml.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Morphine Sulfate:</li>
</ol>
<p>Class.: Narcotic analgesic, morphine type.</p>
<p>Action: See narcotic analgesic.</p>
<p>Uses:</p>
<ul>
<li>Intrathecally, epidurally, orally or I.V. infusion for acute or chronic pain.</li>
<li>Preoperative medication.</li>
<li>To facilitate induction of anesthesia or to decrease the dose of anesthesia.</li>
</ul>
<p>N.B.:</p>
<p>It is given in lower doses for continuous pain &amp; in higher doses in sharp intermittent &amp; all kinds of pain.</p>
<p>Additional contraindications:</p>
<ul>
<li>It is given epidural or intrathecal, if infection is present at injection site.</li>
</ul>

<p><strong>4. Tramadol hydrochloride</strong></p>
<p><strong>Trade name:</strong> Ultram, Tramal</p>
<p><strong>Class.:</strong> Narcotic analgesic, synthetic.</p>
<p><strong>Action:</strong> Unknown. A centrally acting synthetic analgesic compound not chemically related to opiates. Thought to bind to opioid receptors and inhibit reuptake of norepinephrine and serotonin.</p>
<p><strong>Indications &amp; dosages</strong></p>
<p>Moderate to moderately severe pain</p>
<p><strong>Adults:</strong> Initially, 25 mg P.O. Adjust by 25 mg q 3 days to 100 mg/day (on divided doses).</p>
<p><strong>Adverse reactions</strong></p>
<p><strong>CNS:</strong> dizziness, vertigo, headache, CNS stimulation, anxiety, confusion, euphoria, nervousness, sleep disorder, seizures, malaise, visual disturbances.</p>
<p><strong>CV:</strong> vasodilation.</p>
<p><strong>GI:</strong> nausea, vomiting, constipation, dyspepsia, dry mouth, diarrhea, abdominal pain, anorexia, flatulence.</p>
<p><strong>GU:</strong> urine retention, urinary frequency, menopausal symptoms, proteinuria.</p>
<p><strong>Respiratory:</strong> respiratory depression.</p>
<p>126</p>
<p><strong>Skin:</strong> pruritus, diaphoresis, rash.</p>
<p><strong>Contraindications &amp; cautions</strong></p>
<p>Contraindicated in patients hypersensitive to drug or other opioids, in breastfeeding women, and in those with acute intoxication from alcohol, hypnotics, centrally acting analgesics, opioids, or psychotropic drugs.</p>
<p>Use cautiously in patients at risk for seizures or respiratory depression; in patients with increased intracranial pressure or head injury, acute abdominal</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>conditions, or renal or hepatic impairment; or in patients with physical dependence on opioids.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Reassess patient's level of pain at least 30 minutes after administration.</li>
<li>Monitor CV and respiratory status. Withhold dose and notify doctor if respirations decrease or rate is below 12 breaths/minute.</li>
<li>Monitor bowel and bladder function. Anticipate need for laxative.</li>
<li>For better analgesic effect, give drug before onset of intense pain.</li>
<li>Monitor patients at risk for seizures. Drug may reduce seizure threshold.</li>
<li>In the case of an overdose, naloxone may also increase risk of seizures.</li>
<li>Monitor patient for drug dependence. Drug can produce dependence similar to that of codeine and thus has potential for abuse.</li>
<li>Withdrawal symptoms may occur if drug is stopped abruptly. Reduce dosage gradually.</li>
<li>Caution ambulatory patient to be careful when rising and walking. Warn outpatient to avoid driving and other potentially hazardous activities that require mental alertness until drug's CNS effects are known.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="narcotic-antagonists">Narcotic Antagonists:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#narcotic-antagonists" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The narcotic antagonists are able to prevent or reverse many of the pharmacological actions of morphine-type analgesics &amp; meperedine as respiratory depression induced by these drugs within minutes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="naloxone-hydrocholride">Naloxone Hydrocholride:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#naloxone-hydrocholride" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Trade name: Narcan.</p>
<p>Class.: Narcotic antagonist.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="action">Action:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Block the action of narcotic analgesic by displacing previously given narcotics from their receptor sites or preventing them from attaching to opiate receptors.</li>
<li>The duration of action of naloxone is shorter than that of the narcotic analgesic so the respiratory depression may return when the narcotic antagonist has washed off the body.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Respiratory depression induced by narcotics.</li>
<li>Drug of choice when the depressant drug is unknown.</li>
<li>Diagnosis of acute opiate overdose.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>N.B.: Naloxine is not effective when respiratory depression is induced by hypnotic, sedative or other nonarcotic drugs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications">Contraindications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Sensitivity to drug.</li>
<li>Narcotic addicts since it will cause severe withdrawal symptoms.</li>
<li>Neonates.</li>
</ul>
<p>128</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Nausea, vomiting, sweating, hypertension, tremors.</li>
<li>If used postoperatively: tachycardia, pulmonary edema, hypo or hypertension.</li>
</ul>
<p>Dose: 0.4-2 mg I.V., S.C. or I.M.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1- Determine the etiology of respiratory depression.
2- Assess &amp; obtain baseline vital signs.
3- Monitor respiration closely after the duration of action.
4- Have emergency drugs &amp; equipment available.
5- If the patient is comatosed, turn him to his side to avoid aspiration.
6- Maintain safe environment (side rails &amp; soft support).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="non-narcotic-analgesics-antipyretics">Non-narcotic Analgesics &amp; Antipyretics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#non-narcotic-analgesics-antipyretics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Drugs such as aspirin and acetaminophen are available without a prescription, thus consumed in large quantities for the relief of pain and fever.</li>
<li>If they were used improperly, their administration may cause serious effects.</li>
<li>They are responsible for accidental poisoning in small children.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="salicylates">Salicylates:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#salicylates" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-acetylsalicylic-acid">1. Acetylsalicylic Acid:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-acetylsalicylic-acid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Trade name: Aspirin</p>
<p>Classification: Non-narcotic analgesic, antipyretic, anti-inflammatory, antirhumatic, antiplatelet, NSAID.</p>
<p>129</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="action">Action:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The antipyretic effect is due to an action on the hypothalamus that results in heat loss by vasodilation of peripheral blood vessels &amp; promoting sweating.</li>
<li>The anti-inflammatory effects probably by decreasing prostaglandin synthesis &amp; other mediators of the pain response.</li>
<li>The analgesic action is not fully known but may be due to improvement of the inflammatory condition.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>N.B.: Aspirin also produces inhibition of platelet aggregation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Pain - Myalgia</li>
<li>Arthralgia - Headache</li>
<li>Dysmenorrhea - Antipyretic (reduce fever)</li>
<li>Anti-inflammatory (arthritis, gout, rheumatic fever)</li>
<li>To reduce the risk of recurrent ischemic attacks &amp; strokes in men.</li>
<li>Reduction of risk of death or nofatal MI in patients with history of infarction or unstable angina pectoris.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dose">Dose:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>In minor conditions: 325-600 mg Q 4 hours.</li>
<li>May reach up to 6 grams/day in divided doses in arthritis and rheumatic conditions.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications">Contraindications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypersensitivity to salicylates.</li>
<li>Asthma in conjunction with anticoagulant therapy.</li>
<li>Vitamin deficiency (risk for bleeding increase with Vitamin K deficiency).</li>
</ul>
<p>130</p>
<ul>
<li>Chickenpox or influenza (potential risk for Reye’s syndrome among children and teenagers).</li>
<li>Pregnancy and lactation.</li>
<li>One week before &amp; after surgery.</li>
<li>Patients receiving anticoagulants.</li>
<li>Patients with bleeding disorders (ie, hemophilia)</li>
<li>GI bleeding or hemorrhage from other sites.</li>
<li>History of GI ulcers.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Children with chicken pox (Rays syndrom).</li>
<li>Heartburn, nausea, anorexia, occult blood loss..</li>
<li>GI bleeding, potentiation of peptic ulcer.</li>
<li>Bronchospasm.</li>
<li>Anaphylaxis</li>
<li>Skin rashes.</li>
<li>Increase bleeding time.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="salicylate-toxicity">Salicylate toxicity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#salicylate-toxicity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Salicylism: nausea, vomiting, dizziness, tinnitus, difficulty hearing, diarrhea, mental confusion.</li>
<li>Acute aspirin poisoning: Metabolic acidosis, Respiratory alkalosis, hyperpnea, tachypnea, hemorrhage, confusion, pulmonary edema,</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="drug-interactions">Drug interactions:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-interactions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Risk for bleeding increase if taken with other anticoagulants.</li>
<li>Risk of GI bleeding increase if taken with steroids, alcohol, or other NSAIDs.</li>
<li>Increased risk for salicylate toxicity if taken with frusimide (lasix)</li>
</ul>
<p>131</p>
<ul>
<li>Hypotension may occur if taken with nitroglycerins.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Take drug with or after food or with milk to decrease GI irritation.</li>
<li>Assess for history of asthma and history of hypersensitivity.</li>
<li>Do not use with other anticoagulants.</li>
<li>Note any history of peptic ulcer.</li>
<li>Report signs of side effect e.g. gastric irritation if occurs.</li>
<li>Aspirin is not given 1 week before &amp; after surgery to prevent bleeding.</li>
<li>If patient is diabetic, discuss the possibility of hypoglycemia occurring.</li>
<li>Patients should monitor their blood glucose level frequently.</li>
<li>Teaches patient about the toxic symptoms (ringing in the ears, dizziness, mental confusion-etc) and ask him/her to report it to physician.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-acetaminophen-paracetamol">2. Acetaminophen: "paracetamol"<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-acetaminophen-paracetamol" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Trade names: acamol, panadol
Class.: non-narcotic analgesic, antipyretic.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="action">Action:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Acetaminophen decrease fever by an effect on hypothalamus leading to vasodilation &amp; sweating.</li>
<li>It also inhibits the effect of pyrogens on the heat-regulating center on the hypothalamus.</li>
<li>It may cause analgesia by inhibiting CNS prostaglandin syntheses. So it has no anti-inflammatory effect.</li>
<li>It doesn't manifest any anticoagulant effect or any ulceration of GIT.</li>
</ul>
<p>132</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Pain due to Headache, dysmenorrhea, arthralgia, myalgia, musculoskeletal pain, immunization, teething, tonsillectomy.</li>
<li>To reduce fever due to bacterial &amp; viral infection.</li>
<li>As a substitute for aspirin when contraindicated.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications-renal-insufficiency-anemia">Contraindications: renal insufficiency, anemia.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications-renal-insufficiency-anemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Chronic &amp; even acute toxicity can occur after long symptom-free usage.</li>
<li>Heamolytic anemia, neutrtopnea, thrombocytopnea</li>
<li>Skin rashes, fever, jaundice, hypoglycemia.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="symptoms-of-over-dosage">Symptoms of over dosage:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms-of-over-dosage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Hepatic toxicity general malaise, nausea, vomiting, fever, and vascular collapse, delirium, depression, seizures, coma &amp; death.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-overdose">Treatment of overdose:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-overdose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1- Induction of emesis.
2- Gastric lavage.
3- Activated charcoal.
4- Oral N-acetyleystine (mucomyst) is said to reduce or prevent hepatic damage by inactivating acetaminophen metabolites which cause liver effects.</p>
<p>Dose: Tab. 500 mg Q 4 hrs or up to 1g Q 6 hrs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

2- Liver function studies for long term therapy.
3- Have mucomyst available for signs of toxicity.
4- Teach patient signs of toxicity to be reported immediately.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="action">Action:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As in aspirin, the therapeutic actions of these substances are believed to result from the inhibition of the enzyme cyclo-oxygenase which results in decreased prostaglandin synthesis so it is effective in:</p>
<ul>
<li>Reducing joint swelling, pain &amp; morning stiffness.</li>
<li>Increasing the mobility in arthritic patients.</li>
<li>Antipyretic action due to decreased production of prostaglandin from the hypothalamus.</li>
<li>Having irritating effect on the GIT.</li>
</ul>

<p><strong>Nursing considerations:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Note any history of allergic responses to aspirin or nonsteroidal antiinflammatory agents. {NS.AID.}</li>
<li>Note the age of the client.</li>
<li>Determine if patient is taking oral hypoglycemic or insulin and document it.</li>
<li>Take these agents with milk or meal or antacids as prescribed.</li>
<li>Encourage patient to take drug regularly.</li>
<li>Report signs of GI irritation.</li>
<li>Instruct client to report signs of bleeding, blurring of vision, tinnitis, rashes – etc.</li>
<li>If the client has Diabetes Mellitus, explain the possible in increasing hypoglycemic effect of the drugs, to test urine &amp; blood for glucose to adjust dose of these agents.</li>
</ol>

135</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="drugs-affecting-the-autonomic-nervous-system">Drugs Affecting the Autonomic Nervous System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drugs-affecting-the-autonomic-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sympathomimetic (Adrenergic) Drugs</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The adrenergic drugs supplement, mimic &amp; reinforce the message transmitted by the natural neurohormones norepinephrine &amp; epinephrine.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>These hormones are responsible for transmitting nerve impulses of the sympathetic nervous system.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The adrenergic drugs work in 2 ways:</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>
<p>By mimicking the action of epinephrine and norepinephrine (directly).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>By regulating the release of the natural neurohormones from their storage sites at the never terminals (indirectly aching).</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>136</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The myoneural junction is equipped with special receptors for the neurohormones.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>These receptors are classified into: alpha receptor and Beta (β) receptors) according to weather they respond to epinephrine, norepinephrine &amp; to certain blocking agents.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Alpha receptors are blocked by phentolamine. Where beta-receptors are blocked by propranolol &amp; semilar agents.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Both alpha and beta receptors have been divided into subtypes:</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="alpha-receptors">Alpha receptors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#alpha-receptors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Alpha 1 - adrenergic alpha 2 - adrenergic</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Vasoconstriction (of skin - insulin secretion blood vessels).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Decongestion - motility + secretion of GIT</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dilatation of eye pupil</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Contraction of urinary bladder sphincter</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="beta-receptors">Beta receptors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#beta-receptors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>137</p>
<p>Beta 1 - adrenergic Beta 2 - adrenergic</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Increase Myocardial contraction</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Skeletal &amp; coronary vasodilation</p>
</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects-of-adrenergic-drugs">Effects of adrenergic drugs:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-adrenergic-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Heart: increase Heart rate, increase force of contraction, increase cardiac output.
Uses: cardiogenic shock, bradycardia, resuscitation, heart block.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Blood vessels: - Systemic vasoconstriction decrease blood supply to abdominal viscera, cerebrum &amp; skin.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>B.P. in Large vessels increased &amp; regulated.
Uses: Hypotension, nasal decongestion, biliary colic, nose bleeds, migraine, headache, allergic reactions.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>
<p>GI + GU tracts: decrease glandular secretions, constriction of sphincters, decrease muscle tone &amp; motility of GIT &amp; urinary bladder, increase muscle tone &amp; motility of the ureters.
✧ Uses: Enuresis, dysmenarrhea, biliary colic.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lungs: Relaxation of muscles of bronchial tree.
✧ Uses: Bronchial asthma, emphysema, chronic bronchitis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Eyes: Dilate iris, increase ocular pressure, relaxes ciliary muscle.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>CNS: Excitory action, Respiratory stimulation, wakefulness.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Metabolism: increase in glycogenesis (sugar metabolism). Increase in lypolysis (release of fatty acids).</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="drugs">Drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Albuterol: salbutoml
Trade name: ventolin
Class.: sympathomimetic agent, bronchdialtor
Action: stimulate β 2 receptors of the bronchi leading to bronchodilation.</li>
</ol>
<p>Uses:</p>
<ul>
<li>Bronchial asthma.</li>
<li>Bronchospasm due to bronchitis or emphysema.</li>
<li>Parenteral for treatment of status asthmaticus.</li>
</ul>
<p>Dosage:
Aerosol for inhalation: 0.18 – 0.2 mg (2 inhalations) Every 4 – 8 hours.
Solution for inhalation: 1.25 mg in 2 – 5 ml.
Oral syrup, tablets: 2 – 6 mg tid – qid.</p>
<p>Side effects:
Tachycardia, arrhythmias, anginal pain.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Nausea, vomiting.
Dizziness, sweating, flushing.
Headache, weakness, vertigo, and insomnia.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Don't exceed the recommended dose.</li>
<li>The contents of the container are under pressure, don't store near heat or open flames.</li>
<li>When given by neubilization, use facemask or mouth-piece.</li>
<li>Compress O2 or air at 6 – 10 L/min for 5-15 minutes.</li>
<li>Observe client for evidence of allergic response.</li>
<li>NEVER give the solution prepared to be given as inhalation by the IV route. It may cause severe tachycardia.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-epinephrine">2) Epinephrine:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-epinephrine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Trade name:</strong> Adrenaline
<strong>Class.:</strong> Direct acting-adrenergic agent.</p>
<p><strong>Action:</strong>
A natural hormone produced from adrenal medulla, induce marked stimulation of alpha, β1 + β2 receptors causing cardiac stimulation, bronchodilation &amp; decongestion.</p>
<p><strong>Uses:</strong>
1- Relief of respiratory distress due to bronchospasm.
2- Rapid relief of hypersensitivity reactions.
3- Cardiac arrest.
4- Open- angle glaucoma.
5- To prolong the action of anesthesia.
6- Topically to stop bleeding.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications">Contraindications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Narrow angle glaucoma.</li>
<li>Shock</li>
<li>Lactation.</li>
<li>Tachycardia</li>
<li>During labor (it may delay the 2nd 8 loge do labor).</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Never administer 1: 100 solution IV., use 1 : 1000 mg sol. For I.V. use.</li>
<li>Use insulin (1cc) syringe to measure adrenaline.</li>
<li>Administer adrenaline using piggyback set to adjust the rate of infusion.</li>
<li>Administer infusion by electronic infusion device for safety &amp; accuracy.</li>
<li>Closely monitor patients receiving I.V. adrenaline infusion.</li>
<li>Note the client for signs of shock —loss of consciousness, clammy, cold skin, cyanosis... etc.).</li>
<li>Briskly massage site of S.C. or I.M. injection to hasten the action of the drug.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cholinergic-blocking-parasympatholytic-drugs">Cholinergic Blocking (Parasympatholytic) Drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cholinergic-blocking-parasympatholytic-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="action">Action:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These agents prevent the neurotransmitter acetylcholine from combining with receptors on the muscarinic site &amp; nicotonic site.</p>
<p>141</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-main-effects">The main effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-main-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1- Reduce spasm of smooth muscle such as spasm of the urinary bladder or intestines.
2- To block vagal impulses to the heart which will increase heart rate &amp; conductivity.
3- To suppress or decrease gastric secretions, perspiration, salivation and secretion of bronchial mucus.
4- To relax the sphincter muscles of the iris &amp; cause pupillary dilation (mydriasis) &amp; loss of accommodation for near vision.
5- Act on CNS producing such reactions as depression (scoplamine) or stimulation (toxic dose of atropine) to produce antiparkinsonism effect.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications">Contraindications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Glaucoma, tachycardia, myocardial ischemia</p>
<p>Prostate hypertrophy, myasthenia gravis, paralytic ileus,</p>
<p>Mental impairment, lactation, hepatic disease.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-atropine-sulfate">1) Atropine sulfate:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-atropine-sulfate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Class.:</strong> Cholinergic blocking agent.</p>
<p><strong>Action:</strong></p>
<p>It is a parasympatholytic agent which cause relaxation of smooth muscles &amp; inhibition of secretary glands: — See parasympatholyhtic||.</p>
<p>142</p>
<p><strong>Uses:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Adjunct in peptic ulcer treatment.</li>
<li>Irritable bowel syndrome.</li>
<li>Treatment of spastic disorders of biliary tract.</li>
<li>During anesthesia to control salivation &amp; bronchial secretions.</li>
<li>Parkinsonism.</li>
<li>Anti-arrhythmic (prophylaxis).</li>
<li>Prophylaxis and treatment of toxicity due to cholinesterase inhibitor including organophosphate pesticides.</li>
<li>Ophthalmologic treatment of uveitis.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Contraindications:</strong> See parasympatholytics</p>
<p><strong>Side effects:</strong> See parasympatholytics</p>
<p><strong>Dose:</strong></p>
<p>Tablets: 0.3 – 1.2 mg Q 4-6 hr</p>
<p>Available in 1ml-ampoule containing 1 mg atropine.||</p>
<p>IM, I.V. &amp; S.C. 0.4 – 0.6 mg Q 4-6 hour for anticholinergic action.</p>
<p><strong>N.B. :</strong></p>
<p>For treatment of toxicity from cholinesterase inhibitors — organophosphorus poisoning ||, give 2-4 mg IV initially then 2 mg every 5-10 minutes until muscarinic symptoms disappear and signs of atropine toxicity begins to appear like dilation of pupils, flushing of face &amp; tachycardia.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Check dosage &amp; measure the drug exactly.</li>
<li>Assess for history of asthma, glaucoma, ulcer .. etc.</li>
<li>Determine the age of the client.</li>
<li>Frequent mouth care.</li>
</ul>
<p>143</p>
<ul>
<li>Assess client for change in pulse rate.</li>
<li>In case of blurring of vision, assist on ambulating &amp; give safety measures.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-scopalamine-hydrobromide">2) Scopalamine Hydrobromide :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-scopalamine-hydrobromide" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Class.: cholinergic blocking agent.</p>
<p><strong>Action:</strong>
It is a parasympatholytic agent, depress the cerebral cortex, especially the motor area, act as a powerful hypnotic.</p>
<p><strong>Uses:</strong>
1- Motion sickness (prevention and control of nausea and vomiting).
2- Preanesthetic.
3- Antiarrhythmic.
4- Mydriatic and cycloplegic.
5- Adjunctive with other drugs to treat GIT ulcers.
6- With other narcotics to treat biliary colic.</p>
<p><strong>Contraindications:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Hypersensitivity. - Glaucoma</li>
<li>Bronchial asthma - Cardiac arrhythmias</li>
</ul>
<table><thead><tr><th>- Pregnancy</th><th>- Lactation.</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Dose:</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Oral: 0.25 mg I hour before travel (for motion sickness).
Parenteral: 0.32-0.6 mg SC or IM.</p>
<p><strong>Side effects:</strong>
Pupil dilation, photophobia, blurred vision, headache, drowsiness.
Dry mouth, constipation, nausea, vomiting.</p>
<p>144</p>
<p>tachycardia, arrhythmia
Suppression of lactation, flushing, nasal congestion.</p>
<p><strong>Nursing considerations:</strong>
As atropine.</p>
<p>Antihistamines —H1 Blockers</p>
<ul>
<li>Histamine is stored in almost every type of tissue in the body.</li>
<li>Appropriate stimuli including: tissue injury, antigen-antibody (allergic) reactions, and extreme cold trigger the release of histamine from its storage sites into the vascular system where it induces the following responses:
1- Dilation &amp; increased permeability of the small arterioles &amp; capillaries results in increasing permeability to fluid leading to hypotension &amp; edema, nasal congestion &amp; laryngeal edema —associated with allergies.
2- Contraction of some smooth muscles such as those of bronchioles leading to bronchoconstriction —the role of histamine plays in bronchial asthma &amp; Uterine contraction.
3- Stimulation of acid secretion in the stomach &amp; salivary, bronchoial &amp; intestinal secretions.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>4- Dilation of cerebral vessels headache.
5- Pain &amp; itching because it stimulates the sensory nerve endings.</p>
<p><strong>Action:</strong> —of antihistamines</p>
<p>➤ The effect of histamines may be reversed either by drugs that block histamine receptors (antihistamine) or by drugs that have effects opposite to those of histamine e.g. epinephrine.</p>
<p>145</p>
<p>➤ Antihistamines used for the treatment of allergic conditions are referred to as H1-receptor blockers while those used for treatment of GI disorders as peptic ulcer are referred as H2-receptor blockers.</p>
<p>➤ They don’t prevent the release of histamine</p>
<p>➤ They prevent or reduce increased permeability edema &amp; itching, &amp; bronchospasm.</p>
<p>➤ H1-blockers manifest varying degrees of CNS depression, anticholinergic &amp; antiemetic effect.</p>
<p><strong>Uses:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Treatment of seasonal allergic rhinitis, allergic conjunctivitis.</li>
<li>Treatment of urticarial transfusion reactions.</li>
<li>Treatment of topic dermatitis.</li>
<li>Treatment of insect bites.</li>
<li>Sneezing &amp; rhinorrhea due to common cold.</li>
<li>Prophylaxis &amp; treatment of motion sickness —nausea &amp; vomiting||.</li>
<li>Night – time sleep aid.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Contraindications:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Hypersensitivity.</li>
<li>Pregnancy.</li>
<li>Glaucoma</li>
<li>Prostatic hypertrophy</li>
<li>CNS depression (phenothiazine type).</li>
<li>Bone marrow depression</li>
<li>Comatose patients.</li>
</ul>
<p>146</p>
<p><strong>Side effects:</strong></p>
<p>➤ Sedation - deep sleep - Dizziness - Headache - muscle weakness - disturbed coordination - epigastric distress - dry mouth - nausea - vomiting - urinary frequency, anemia (pancytopnea).</p>
<p>➤ Paradoxical excitation (especially in children &amp; elderly)
Restlessness, irritability, insomnia, hysteria, tremors, euphoria, nervousness, hallucinations, disorientation &amp; convulsion.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-overdose">Treatment of overdose:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-overdose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptomatic &amp; supportive.</li>
<li>Vomiting is induced with syrup of ipecac.</li>
<li>Gastric laavage.</li>
<li>Vasopressors (to treat hypotension) –e.g. Dopamine, adrenaline.</li>
<li>Phenytoin for treatment of convulsion.</li>
</ul>
<p>N.B.: Don't use CNS depressants including diazepam.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing Considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Inject I.M. preparations deep into muscles.</li>
<li>Oral preparations may cause gastric irritation, so give drug with meals.</li>
<li>Note if the client has any medical history of ulcer, glaucoma &amp; if the client is pregnant.</li>
<li>Obtain a baseline B.P., Pulse &amp; respiration.</li>
<li>Note signs of CNS depression (signs of overdose so induce vomiting).</li>
<li>If in hospital, use side rails (safety measures).</li>
<li>Advice client to report signs of side effects immediately.</li>
<li>Instruct client to avoid undue exposure to sun.</li>
</ul>
<p>147</p>
<ul>
<li>If the drug is being used for motion sickness, it should be taken 30 minutes before transporting.</li>
<li>Caution the client not to drive a car or operate other machinery.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="drugs-in-this-group">*Drugs in this group:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drugs-in-this-group" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-promethazine-hcl">2- Promethazine Hcl:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-promethazine-hcl" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><strong>Trade name:</strong> phenergan, prothiazine.
<strong>Class.:</strong> It is a potent antihistamine with prolonged action. It may cause severe drowsiness. It also provides antiemetic effect (it chemo receptor trigger zone).</p>
<p>It also has a sedative action, effective in vertigo vestibular apparatus</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Motion sickness.</li>
<li>Nausea &amp; vomiting due to anesthesia.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="forms">Forms:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#forms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Syrup:</strong> 5ml contains 5 mg, 25 mg.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Ampule: 50 mg \ 2ml.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dose">Dose:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
