<p>148</p>
<p>Sedative: 25 mg – 50 mg.</p>
<p>Antivertigo: 25 mg 2 times daily.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hormones-hormone-antagonists">Hormones &amp; Hormone Antagonists<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hormones-hormone-antagonists" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="insulin">Insulin:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#insulin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; 2 main hormones are secreted from the pancreas :</p>
<p>1- Insulin which is secreted by β-cells of islets of langerhans &amp; stored in the pancreas (β-.cells) as a large protein known as proinsulin.</p>
<p>2- Glucagon which is thought to oppose the action of insulin. It is secreted by the α cells of islets of langerhans, it converts glycogen to glucose &amp; elevates blood glucose level.</p>
<p>&gt; Diabetes mellitus is a disease in which the islets of langerhans in the pancreas produce either no insulin or insufficient quantities of insulin. It is classified as insulin dependent (type 1 or juvenileonset) &amp; noninsulin dependent (type II or maturity -onset).</p>
<p>&gt; It can be treated successfully by the administration of insulin isolated from the pancreas of cattle or hogs or of human insulin made either semisynthetically or derived from recombinant DNA technology.</p>
<p>&gt; The structure of insulin from pork - sources more closely resembles human insulin than that from beef sources.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="insulin">Insulin:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#insulin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1- Rapid-acting insulin.</p>
<p>One) Insulin injection (regular, crystalline zinc insulin).</p>
<p>Two) Prompt insulin zinc suspension.</p>
<p>2- Intermediate-acting insulin</p>
<p>149</p>
<p>One) Isophane insulin suspension (NPH)</p>
<p>Two) Insulin zinc suspension (lente)</p>
<p>3- Long-acting insulin</p>
<p>Un) Protamine zinc insuline suspension (PZI)</p>
<p>Deux) Extended insuline zinc suspension (ultralente)</p>
<p>N.B. : Insulin preparations with various times of onset &amp; duration of action are often mixed to obtain optimum control in diabetic patients.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="action">Action:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1- Facilitates the transport of glucose into cardiac &amp; skeletal muscles</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>&amp; adipose tissue.</p>
<p>2- Increases synthesis of glycogen in the liver.
3- Stimulates protein synthesis &amp; lipogenesis.
4- Inhibits lipolysis &amp; release of free fatty acids from fat cells.
5- Causes intracellular shifts of potassium.</p>
<p>N.B.: Since insulin is a protein, it is destroyed in the GIT thus it must be administered parenterally.</p>
<ul>
<li>It is metabolized mainly in the liver.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Replacement therapy in type I diabetes.</li>
<li>Indicated in type II diabetes when other measures have failed or with surgery, trauma, infection, fever, endocrine dysfunction, pregnancy, gangrene, kidneys or liver disease.</li>
<li>Regular insulin is used in I.V. hyperalimentation.</li>
<li>Regular insulin is used in I.V. dextrose to treat sever hyperkalemia.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications">Contraindications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Hypersensitivity to insulin.</p>
<p>150</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1- Hypoglycemia due to overdose, decreased food intake or hard exercise, — Hunger, weakness, fatigue, nervousness, pallor or flushing, profuse sweating, headache, numbness of mouth, tingling in the fingers, blurred vision, hypothermia &amp; loss of consciousness.
—Sever prolonged hypoglycemia may cause brain damage.
2- Allergic urticaria, lymphadenopathy. — Use human Insulin product.
3- At the site of injection :- developing of swelling, itching, atrophy or hypertrophy of S.C. fat tissue so rotate site of injection to minimize the problem.
4- Insulin resistance caused by obesity, infection, trauma, surgery ...etc.
5- Hyperglycemic rebound (somogyi effect) in patients who receive chronic overdose.</p>
<p>&gt; Diabetic coma is usually precipitated by the patient's failure to take insulin.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-diabetic-coma">*** Treatment of diabetic coma:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-diabetic-coma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; 20 – 30 units of insulin, then 20 units every 30 minutes.
&gt; To avoid hypoglycemia give 1 g dextrose for each unit of insulin is administered with supplemental electrolytes (K+) &amp; fluids.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>&gt; Monitor vital signs.
&gt; Urine samples for analysis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-hypoglycemia">Treatment of hypoglycemia:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-hypoglycemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>151</p>
<ul>
<li>Mild hypoglycemia: relieved by oral administration of CHO as orange juice.</li>
<li>In comatosed patients: administer 10–30 ml of 50% dextrose solution I.V.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dose">Dose:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Usually administered S.C.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="n-b">N.B.:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#n-b" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; Regular insulin is the <strong>ONLY</strong> preparation that may be administered I.V
&gt; This route should be used only for patients with severe ketoacidosis or diabetic coma.
&gt; Always expressed in units.
&gt; Dosage is individualized, it is established &amp; monitored by blood glucose, urine glucose &amp; acetone test.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="insulin-antagonists">Insulin antagonists:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#insulin-antagonists" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1- Growth hormone elevates glucose level &amp; decreases glycogen synthesis.
2- Glucocorticoids enhance conversion of protein to glucose.
3- Adrenaline decreases insulin release &amp; enhance glycogenolysis.
4- Thyroid hormone promote gluconeogenesis.
5- Glucagon.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1- Read the product information &amp; any important notes inserted into the package.
2- Refrigerate stock supply of insulin but avoid freezing.
3- Follow the guidelines with respect to mixing the various types of insulin.</p>
<p>152</p>
<p>4- Invert the vial several times to mix before the material is withdrawn —avoid vigorous shaking|.
5- Assist patient for self-administration of insulin.
6- Rotate the sites of S.C. injections to prevent the problem of hypertrophy or atrophy at injection site.
7- Allow insulin to remain at room temperature 1 hour before administration.
8- Apply pressure for 1 minute, don’t massage since it may interfere with rate of absorption.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>9- If breakfast must be delayed, delay the administration of morning dose of insulin.
10- Obtain a thorough nursing history from the client / family.
11- If the client has symptoms of hyperglycemia reaction:</p>
<ul>
<li>Have regular insulin available for administration.</li>
<li>Monitor client closely after administration.</li>
<li>Check blood glucose, urine glucose, and acetone.
12- Check for early symptoms of hypoglycemia.
13- Assess diabetic more closely for infection or emotional disturbances that may increase insulin requirements.
14- Explain the necessity for close regular medical supervision.
15- Explain to patient how to test the urine for sugar &amp; acetone.
16- Explain the use &amp; care of equipment &amp; the storage of medication.
17- Explain the importance of exercise &amp; adhering to the prescribed diet.
18- Explain the importance of carrying candy or sugar at all times to counteract hypoglycemia should it occur.</li>
</ul>
<p>153</p>
<p>19- Provide the client &amp; family with a printed chart explaining symptoms of hypoglycemia, hyperglycemia &amp; instructions concerning what to do for each.
20- Instruct client that blurring of vision will subside within 6-8 weeks.
21- Advise client to check vials of insulin carefully before each dose.
22- Regular insulin should be clear, where as other forms may be cloudy.</p>
<p>1- Insulin Injection (Regular, crystalline Zinc insulin)</p>
<p>Class: Rapid- acting insulin.</p>
<p>Kinetics:
Onset ½ -1 hr (S.C), 10-30m (I.V.).
Peak 2-4 hr (S.C), 15-30m (I.V.).
Duration 5-7 hr (S.C), 30-60m (I.V.).</p>
<p>Uses: suitable for treatment of diabetic coma, acidosis (diabetic) or other emergency situations.
Dose: individualized, initial 5-10 units 15-30 minutes before meals &amp; at bedtime.
Diabetic acidosis 0.1 unit / kg given by continuous I.V. infusion.</p>
<p>2- Isophane Insulin Injection (NPH):
N = neutral solution P= stand of PZI
H= means that it is originated in Hagedron’s laboratory.
Class: Intermediate – acting insulin.
Kinetics: onset 3-4 hr, duration 18-28 hr.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Peak 6-12 hr.</p>
<p>154</p>
<p>Dose: S.C. Individualized, initial 7-26 units as a single dose 30-60 minutes before breakfast.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="oral-antidiabetic-hypoglycemic-agents">Oral Antidiabetic (Hypoglycemic) Agents<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#oral-antidiabetic-hypoglycemic-agents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Several oral antidiabetic agents are available for patients with noninsulin dependent diabetes.</li>
<li>Oral hypoglycemic agents are classified as either first or second generation.</li>
<li>Generation refers to structural changes in the basic molecule.</li>
<li>Second-generation oral hypoglycemic agents are more lipophilic &amp; have greater hypoglycemic potency (200 times) than first generation.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification">Classification:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1- First-generation sulfonylureas compounds such as:
a) Tolbutamide (orinase).
b) Chlorpromide (diabenase).
c) Glibenclamide (Daonil).</p>
<p>2- Second-generation sulfonylureas compounds such as:</p>
<ul>
<li>Glyburide (Micronase).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="action-of-oral-antidiabetic-agents">Action of oral antidiabetic agents:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#action-of-oral-antidiabetic-agents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1- Increases the sensitivity of pancreatic islet cells.
2- Increases insulin secretion by <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>β</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\beta</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.05278em;">β</span></span></span></span></span> cells.
3- The peripheral tissues become more sensitive to insulin due to an increase in the number of insulin receptors &amp; increase the insulin ability to combine with receptors.</p>
<p>155</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indication">Indication:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Non-insulin dependent diabetes mellitus (NIDDM) (type II).</p>
<p>&gt; Patients should be subjected to a 7 day therapeutic trial.
&gt; Decrease in blood sugar, decrease in glucosuria &amp; disappearance of polyuria, polydipsia, &amp; polyphagia indicate that patient can be managed on oral antidiabetic agents.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications">Contraindications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Type I of D.M.</li>
<li>Renal &amp; liver disease.</li>
<li>Diabetes complicated by recurrent episodes of ketoacidosis.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypoglycemia (most common).</li>
<li>Nausea, heartburn, diarrhea</li>
<li>Headache, dizziness, general weakness.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adverse-reactions">Adverse reactions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adverse-reactions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; GI: diarrhea, nausea, vomiting, abdominal bloating, flatulence, anorexia, taste perversion.</p>

<p>&gt; Hematologic: megaloblastic anemia.
&gt; Metabolic: lactic acidosis.
&gt; May decrease vitamin B12 and hemoglobin levels.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications-cautions">Contraindications &amp; cautions:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications-cautions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; Contraindicated in patients hypersensitive to drug and in those with renal disease, hepatic disease, metabolic acidosis, or heart disease.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Assess patient's renal function.</li>
<li>Give with meals; give once-daily dosage with breakfast and twicedaily dosage with breakfast and dinner.</li>
<li>Monitor patient closely during times of increased stress, such as infection, fever, surgery, or trauma. Insulin therapy may be needed in these situations.</li>
<li>Alert: Stop drug immediately and notify doctor if patient develops a condition related to hypoxemia or dehydration because of risk of lactic acidosis.</li>
<li>Monitor patient's hematologic status for evidence of megaloblastic anemia.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adrenocorticosteroids-and-analogs">Adrenocorticosteroids and analogs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adrenocorticosteroids-and-analogs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="action">Action:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>They are a group of natural hormones produced by the adrenal cortex.</li>
<li>They are used for a variety of therapeutic purposes.</li>
</ul>
<p>158</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Many slightly modified synthetic variants are available today.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Some patients respond better to one substance than to another.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>These hormones influence many metabolic pathways &amp; all organ systems &amp; are essential for survival.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The release of corticosteroids is controlled by hormones such as corticotropin-releasing factor produced by the hypothalamus &amp; ACTH produced by the anterior pituitary.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Corticosteroids have the following effect:</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>1- CHO metabolism :</p>
<ul>
<li>Deposition of glucose as glycogen in the liver &amp; conversion of glycogen to glucose when needed.(Gluconeogenesis).
2- Protein metabolism: The stimulation of protein loss from many organs.
3- Fat metabolism: The deposition of fatty tissue in facial, abdominal &amp; shoulder regions.
4- Water &amp; electrolyte balance: Alteration of glomerular filtration rate, increase sodium &amp; fluid retention, also affect the excretion of</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>potassium, calcium &amp; phosphorus.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Have anti-inflammatory effect: they decrease prostaglandin synthesis.</li>
<li>The immunosuppressant effect: they decrease number of Tlymphocyte, monocytes, and eosinophils.</li>
<li>They aid the organism to cope with stressful situations e.g. trauma &amp; sever illness.</li>
</ol>
<p>▪ According to their chemical structure, they fall into 2 classes.
1- Glucocorticoids e.g. cortisone &amp; hydrocortisone: - regulate the metabolism of CHO, protein &amp; fat.</p>
<p>159</p>
<p>2- Mineralocorticoids e.g. Aldosteron &amp; desoxycorticosterone.: - increase reabsorption of Na+ (+water) &amp; excretion of potassium &amp; hydrogen.</p>
<p><strong>Uses:</strong></p>
<p>Therapy with glucocorticoids is not curative &amp; many situations should be considered as adjunctive rather than primary therapy:-:</p>
<p>1- Replacement therapy: adrenal insufficiency (Addison's disease).
2- Rheumatic disorders: rheumatoid arthritis &amp; osteoarthritis.
3- Collagen diseases: systemic lupus erythematosus, rheumatic cardiac.
4- Allergic diseases: drug hypersensitivity, urticarial transfusion reaction.
5- Respiratory diseases: bronchial asthma, rhinitis.
6- Ocular diseases: allergic &amp; inflammatory conjunctivitis, keratitis ...
7- Dermatological diseases: psoriasis, contact dermatitis, urticaria.
8- Diseases of the GIT: ulcerative colitis.
9- Nervous system: Myasthenia gravis.
10- Malignancies: leukemia, lymphoma.
11- Nephrotic syndrome.
12- Hematological diseases: hemolytic anemia, thrombocytopenic purpura.
13- Miscellaneous: septic shock, liver cirrhosis, stimulation of surfactant production, prevention of organ rejection.</p>
<p><strong>Contraindications:</strong></p>
<p>1- If infection is suspected (Mask signs &amp; symptoms).
2- Peptic ulcer.
3- Acute glomerulonephritis.
4- Cushing's syndrome.</p>
<p>160</p>
<p>5- Congestive heart failure.
6- Hypertension.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>7- Hyperlipidemia.</p>
<p><strong>Side effects:</strong></p>
<p>&gt; Prolonged therapy may cause cushing-like syndrome &amp; atrophy of the adrenal cortex &amp; subsequent adrenocortical insufficiency.</p>
<p><strong>N.B:</strong> steroid withdrawal syndrome may lead to: anorexia, nausea, vomiting, weight loss, headache myalgia &amp; hypotension.</p>
<p><strong>Side effects include:</strong> Edema, alkalosis, hypokalemia, hypertension, CHF muscle wasting, weakness, osteoporosis, nausea &amp; vomiting. Headache, hypercholesterolemaea, hirsutism, amenorrhea, depression, increase heart rate, hyperglycemia, and peptic ulcer.</p>
<p><strong>Dose:</strong> Highly individualized according to the condition &amp; response of the patient.</p>
<p><strong>N.B.:</strong> It is most important that therapy not be discontinued abruptly.</p>
<p><strong>Nursing Considerations:</strong></p>
<p>1- Administer oral forms with food to minimize ulcerogenic effect.
2- For chronic use, give the smallest dose possible.
3- Corticosteroids should be discontinued gradually if used chronically.
4- Document baseline weight, B.P., Pulse &amp; temperature.
5- Frequently take BP, monitor body weight (signs of Na+ &amp; H2O retention).
6- Periodic serum electrolytes, blood sugar monitoring.
7- Report signs &amp; symptoms of side effects (cushing-like syndrome).
8- Discuss with female client potentials of menstrual difficulties.
9- Instruct the client to take diet high in protein &amp; potassium.</p>
<p>10- Instruct the client to avoid falls &amp; accidents (osteoporosis causes pathological fracture).
11- Remind the client to carry a card identifying the drug being used.
12- Stress the need for regular medical supervision.
13- Advice the client to delay any vaccination while taking these medications (weakened immunity).
14- Explain the need to maintain general hygiene &amp; cleanliness to prevent infection.</p>

<p><strong>Trade name:</strong> celestone.</p>
<p><strong>Class:</strong> Adrenocorticosteroid, synthetic, glucocorticoid type.</p>
<p><strong>Additional Uses:</strong> prevention of respiratory distress syndrome in premature infants</p>
<p><strong>2- Dexamethasone:</strong></p>
<p><strong>Trade name:</strong> dexacort, decort.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-methylergonovine-maleate">1-Methylergonovine Maleate:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-methylergonovine-maleate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Trade name: Methergine.</p>
<p>Class: Oxytocic agent.</p>
<p>Action: Is a synthetic agent stimulates the rate, tone &amp; amplitude of uterine contractions. It also stimulates smooth muscles surrounding certain blood vessels by interacting with adrenergic &amp; dopaminergic receptors.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1- Management &amp; prevention of postpartum hemorrhage by producing firm cervical contractions &amp; decrease uterine bleeding.</p>
<p>2- Incomplete abortion.</p>
<p>3- Migraine headache</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications">Contraindications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Pregnancy - Hypertension</li>
<li>To induce labor - Toxemia</li>
<li>Prior to delivery of placenta</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Nausea, vomiting, diarrhea, allergic reaction, Dizziness, headache, tinnitus, hypertension.</p>
<p>N.B.: use of this substance during labor may result in uterine tetany with rupture, cervical laceration, embolism of amniotic fluid &amp; intracranial hemorrhage in infant.</p>
<p>163</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dose">Dose:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Forms: Tablet 0.2 mg (0.2- 0.4 mg /6-12 hr for 48 hrs).</p>
<p>I.V. in emergency situations.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-oxytocin">2-Oxytocin:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-oxytocin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Trade name: Pitocin</p>
<p>Class: oxytocic agent.</p>
<p>Action:</p>
<ul>
<li>It has uterine stimulant, vasopressive &amp; antidiuretic properties.</li>
<li>Mimics uterine contractions of normal labor.</li>
<li>Facilitates ejection of milk from the breasts by stimulating smooth muscles.</li>
</ul>
<p>Onset: I.V. immediately, I.M 3-5 minutes.</p>
<p>Peak 40 minutes</p>
<p>duration I.V. 20m. I.M. 30-60 m.</p>
<p>Uses:</p>
<ul>
<li>Antepartum induction or stimulation of labor.</li>
<li>Uterine inertia (hypotonic contractions).</li>
<li>For induction of labor in case of preeclampsia, eclampsia, maternal diabetes &amp; other conditions.</li>
<li>To hasten uterine involution.</li>
<li>Intranasally for postpartum hemorrhage &amp; uterine atony.</li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindications:</p>
<ul>
<li>Hypersensitivity - cephalopelvic disproportion (C.P.D.)</li>
<li>Malpreresentation - undilated cervix</li>
<li>History of cesarean delivery.</li>
</ul>
<p>164</p>
<p>N.B.: Oxytocin should never be given I.V. undiluted in high concentration.</p>
<p>Side effects:
Tetanic uterine contraction, rupture uterus Hypertension, tachycardia.</p>
<p>To Fetus: - it may cause death, intracranial hemorrhage, brady or tachycardia</p>
<p>Dose:</p>
<ul>
<li>I.M. or I.V. infusion for induction or stimulation of labor.</li>
<li>I.V. infusion 10 units (1ml) diluted in 1000 ml of normal saline or 5% dextrose</li>
<li>Initial 0.001 – 0.002 unit /minute, increased by small increments after 15 minutes intervals</li>
</ul>
<p>Nursing Considerations:
1- The physician should be available during administration of the drug.
2- Use Y-tubing for I.V. administration (one bottle contain oxytocin &amp; another free).
3- Note any history of hypersensitivity &amp; other contraindications.
4- Check for cervical dilation &amp; uterine contractions patterns.</p>

<p>5- Remain with the client throughout the administration of medication.
6- Monitor fetal heart rate at least every 10 minutes.
7- Check vital signs every 15 minutes.
8- Prevent uterine rupture &amp; fetal damage by stop I.V. oxytocin, start medication – Free fluid, provide O2 &amp; notify the physician in case of hypertonic uterine contraction &amp; abnormal fetal heart rate patterns.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diuretics">Diuretics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diuretics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>165</p>
<p>The kidney is a complex organ with 3 main functions:</p>
<p>1- Maintain the acid-base balance.
2- Elimination of waste materials &amp; return of useful metabolites to the blood.
3- Maintenance of an adequate electrolyte balance, which in turn governs the amount of fluid retained in the body.</p>
<p>&gt; Malfunction of one or more of these regulatory processes may result in the retention of excessive fluid by various tissues (edema).
&gt; Edema is an important manifestation of many conditions such as pregnancy &amp; congestive heart failure.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="action-of-diuretics">Action of diuretics:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#action-of-diuretics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It increase the urinary output of water and sodium —prevention or correction of edema— through one of the following mechanisms:</p>
<p>1- Increasing the glomerular filtration rate.
2- Decreasing the rate at which sodium is reabsorbed from the glomerular filtrate by the renal tubules, therefore water is excreted along with sodium.
3- Promoting the excretion of sodium &amp; therefore water by the kidney.</p>
<p>Uses: Congestive heart failure, hypertension, and edema.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-loop-diuretics">1- Loop Diuretics:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-loop-diuretics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="furosemide">Furosemide<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#furosemide" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Trade name: Fused, Lasix
Class: Loop diuretic.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="action">Action:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>166</p>
<ul>
<li>It inhibits the reabsorption of sodium and chloride in the ascending loop of Henle resulting in the excretion of sodium, chloride &amp; to a lesser degree potassium &amp; bicarbonate ions. Also it decreases the reabsorption of sodium &amp; chloride &amp; increases the excretion of potassium in the distal tubule.</li>
<li>It has a slight antihypertensive effect.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Uses:</p>
<ul>
<li>Edema associated with:</li>
<li>Congestive heart failure</li>
<li>Liver cirrhosis.</li>
<li>Nephrotic syndrome.</li>
<li>Acute pulmonary edema.</li>
<li>Hypertension.</li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindications:</p>
<ul>
<li>Hepatic coma associated with electrolyte depletion.</li>
<li>Anuria</li>
<li>Sever renal diseases.</li>
<li>Hypersensitivity.</li>
</ul>
<p>Side effects:</p>
<ul>
<li>Dehydration, hypovlemia.</li>
<li>Hypokalemia, hyperglycemia, Hyponatremia</li>
<li>Nausea, vomiting, diarrhea, anorexia.</li>
<li>Tinnitus, blurring of vision, headache, orthostatic hypotension, rashes &amp; photosensitivity.</li>
</ul>
<p>*After I.V use: Thrombophlebitis &amp; cardiac arrest.
*After I.M use: pain at injection site.</p>
<p>N.B.:
167
Because the drug potentiates the effects of muscle relaxants, it is recommended to discontinue oral medication 1 week before surgery &amp; the I.V. 2 days before surgery</p>
<p>Forms:
Tablets 40 mg.
Ampules 20 mg /2ml, 250 mg /10 ml.
Dose: oral: 20-80 mg as a single dose.
I.V: 20-40 mg as a single dose.
For hypertensive crisis: 100-200 mg.</p>
<p>Nursing considerations:
1- When high doses are required, administer lasix by infusion.
2- Store in a light-resistant container.
3- Monitor serum electrolytes &amp; for signs of hypokalemia.
4- Observe client for signs of dehydration &amp; circulatory collapse.
5- Monitor pulse &amp; blood pressure.
6- Advise the client to take medication in the morning to avoid interruption of sleep.
7- Discuss the need for a diet high in potassium.</p>

<p>Drugs affecting the respiratory system</p>
<ol>
<li>Antiasthmatic Drugs</li>
</ol>
<p>✧ Theophylline Derivatives:</p>
<p>Action:
They belong to the xanthine family.
They stimulate the CNS, relax the smooth muscles of the bronchi and pulmonary blood vessels which result in relieve bronchospasm.</p>
<p>168
They also have a slight diuretic effect, stimulate gastric acid secretions &amp; increase the force and rate of the heart.</p>
<p>Uses:</p>
<ul>
<li>Prophylaxis and treatment of bronchial asthma.</li>
<li>Reversible bronchospasm associated with C.O.P.D.</li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindications:</p>
<ul>
<li>Hypersensitivity - Hypotension</li>
<li>Coronary artery disease (angina pectoris).</li>
</ul>
<p>Side effects:</p>
<ul>
<li>Nausea, vomiting, epigastric pain.</li>
<li>Rectal irritation following use of suppositories.</li>
<li>Headache, dizziness, Hypotension, arrhythmias (tachycardia)</li>
</ul>
<p>N.B.:
Aminophylline given by rapid I.V. may produce hypotension, flushing, precordial pain, Headache &amp; dizziness.</p>
<p>Overdose:
Toxicity is usually associated with parenteral administration &amp; oral administration especially in children.
Early signs include anorexia, nausea, vomiting, restlessness &amp; irritability.
Later symptom include: agitation, manic behavior, frequent vomiting, extreme thirst &amp; convulsions.</p>
<p>Formulation:
Theophylline derivatives are available as I.V. injections, modified release tablets, capsules, rapid release tablets, syrup, and suppositories.</p>
<p>169
Dose: individualized.</p>
<p>Nursing considerations:
1- Dilute drugs &amp; maintain proper infusion rate.
2- Assess client for any history of hypersensitivity.
3- Obtain baseline blood pressure and pulse prior to starting therapy,</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>monitor B.P. &amp; pulse closely during therapy.</p>
<p>4- Observe closely for signs of toxicity.
5- To avoid epigastric pain (when administered orally) give the medication with meals.
6- Monitor for serum level of theophylline.
7- Instruct the client to increase intake of fluids to liquefy secretions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="examples">Examples:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examples" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-aminophylline">1-Aminophylline:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-aminophylline" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Class: Antiasthmatic, bronchodilator</p>
<p>— Theophylline + ethylenediamine</p>
<p>Action: Relaxes smooth muscles of bronchi causing bronchodilation and increasing vital capacity of the lungs.</p>
<p>Additional use: neonatal apnea and bradycardia.</p>
<p>Forms: Ampule 250 mg/10 ml</p>
<p>Tablets 100mg – 200mg.</p>
<p>Pediatric suppositories: 100mg</p>
<p>I.V. administration: 5mg/kg over a period of 10 - 20 minutes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="dose">Dose:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>IV administration: 250 mg Q 6-8 hours.</p>
<p>Rectal: 500 mg bid.</p>
<p>170</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-theophylline">2- Theophylline:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-theophylline" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="drugs-affecting-the-git">Drugs affecting the GIT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drugs-affecting-the-git" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-antacids">1. Antacids<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-antacids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><strong>Action:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Antacids act by neutralizing or reducing gastric acidity, thus increasing the pH of the stomach and relieving hyperacidity. If the pH is increased to 4, the activity of pepsin is inhibited.</li>
<li>Ideally, antacids should not be absorbed systemically — NaHco3 &amp; CaCo3 may produce systemic effects.</li>
<li>Antacids containing magnesium have a laxative effect.</li>
</ul>
<table><thead><tr><th>- Use s:</th><th>Antacids containing aluminum or calcium have a constipating effect.</th></tr></thead></table>
<ul>
<li>Treatment of hyperacidity. (Heart- burns).</li>
<li>Peptic ulcer</li>
<li>Duodenal ulcer.</li>
</ul>

<p>N.B.: chronic use of aluminum containing antacids may contribute to development of Alzheimer’s disease.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is recommended that most antacids be taken at 3 hours after meals &amp; at bed – time.</li>
<li>Tablets should be thoroughly chewed before swallowing &amp; followed by a glass of milk or water.</li>
<li>Shake liquid suspensions thoroughly before pouring the medication.</li>
<li>Client’s taking aluminum or calcium containing antacids should take 2500-3000 cc of fluids to prevent constipation.</li>
<li>Advise clients to report persistent diarrhea or constipation physician.</li>
</ul>

<strong>Additional uses:</strong> hiatus hernia, Hyperacidity.</p>
<p><strong>Dose:</strong>
2-4 tabs - 20-60 m after meals &amp; at bed time.
Suspension: 10-20 ml aid- 20-60 m after meals &amp; at bed time.</p>

<strong>Class.:</strong> H2-receptor antagonists.</p>
<p><strong>Action:</strong> It competitively inhibits gastric acid secretion by blocking the effect of histamine on histamine H2-receptors.</p>
<p><strong>Uses:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Short-term (up to 8 wks) &amp; maintenance treatment of duodenal ulcer &amp; treatment of benign gastric ulcer.</li>

Dizziness, malaise, vertigo, bradycardia or tachycardia
Pancytopnea, rashes, bronchospasm, alopecia.</p>

Maintenance 150 mg at bed-time.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Dilute for I.V. use (50 mg in 20 ml of 0.9% Nacl).</li>
<li>Note any evidence of renal or liver disease.</li>
<li>Obtain baseline liver &amp; kidney function.</li>
<li>Note for signs of infection.</li>
<li>Adequate hydration for problem of diarrhea.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="action">Action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Inhibits activity of acid (proton) pump and binds to hydrogenpotassium adenosine triphosphatase at secretory surface of gastric parietal cells to block formation of gastric acid.</li>
<li>Dose: 20-40 mg daily for 4-8 weeks</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="glycerin-suppositories">Glycerin Suppositories:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#glycerin-suppositories" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Class</strong>: miscellaneous laxative.
<strong>Action</strong>: promote defecation by irritating the rectal mucosa as well as by hyperosmotic action, It also softens &amp; lubricates fecal material.
<strong>Onset</strong> 15-60 minutes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>To establish normal bowel function in patients dependent on laxatives.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications">Contraindications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Anal fissure, fistula, ulcerative hemorrhoids.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="antiemetics">Antiemetics:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antiemetics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Nausea &amp; vomiting can be caused by a variety of conditions such as infections, drugs, motion, organic disease or psychological factors. The underlying cause of the symptoms must be elicited before emesis is corrected. The act of vomiting is complex. The vomiting center in the medulla responds to stimulation from many peripheral areas as well as stimuli from CNS itself, the CTZ in the medulla, the vestibular apparatus of the ear &amp; the cerebral cortex.</p>
<p>The selection of antiemetic depends on the cause of the symptom as well as on the manner in which the vomiting is triggered.</p>
<p>175
Many drugs used for other conditions such as antihistamine, phenothiazines &amp; barbiturates have antiemetic properties &amp; can be so used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="drug-interaction">Drug interaction:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-interaction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Because of their antiemetic and antinauseant action the antiemetics may mask overdose caused by other drugs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1- Take a complete history, if it is unusual occurrence or if it is a</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>recurring phenomenon.</p>
<p>2- Assess for other untoward symptoms as increased intracranial pressure or intestinal obstruction (antiemetic may mask signs of underlying pathology)
3- Caution the client that drug tends to cause drowsiness &amp; dizziness, advise him\her to avoid hazardous tasks.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="metoclopramide-hcl">Metoclopramide Hcl:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#metoclopramide-hcl" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Trade name:</strong> Pramin</p>
<p><strong>Class:</strong> Antiemetic</p>
<p><strong>Action:</strong> It is dopamine receptor antagonist acts both centrally &amp; peripherally, centrally due to the effect in the CTZ (inhibition), Peripherally it stimulates the motility of the upper GIT without affecting gastric &amp; biliary or pancreatic secretions. It relaxes the pyloric sphincter &amp; increases the peristalsis of the duodenum resulting in accelerated gastric emptying &amp; intestinal transit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indications">Indications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>176</p>
<p>1- Digestive disorders leading to relief GIT pain, Dyspepsia &amp; regurgitation in peptic ulcer, reflux esophagitis &amp; postanasthetic vomiting.
2- Nausea &amp; vomiting as in chemotherapy.
3- Facilitate diagnostic procedure e.g. barium meal.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>GI disturbances, transient hypertension, supraventricular tachycardia, dizziness &amp; extrapyramidal effect —convulsion‖.</p>

2- Administer oral medication 30 minutes before meal &amp; at bed</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="thyroid-antithyroid-drugs">Thyroid &amp; Antithyroid Drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thyroid-antithyroid-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The thyroid manufactures 2 active hormones, thyroxine and Triiodothyronine, both which contain iodine.</p>
<p>Diseases involving the thyroid fall into 2 groups:</p>
<p>1- Hypothyroidism: decreased thyroid hormones.</p>
<ul>
<li>Cretinism in infancy &amp; early life.</li>
<li>Myxedema in adult.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>Cretinism leads to decreasing in physical &amp; mental development.</li>
<li>Myxedema causes: dry swelling, edema (nonpitting)
— primary results from atrophy of the thyroid &amp;
— secondary as a result of hypofunction of pituitary gland or prolonged administration of antithyroid drugs.</li>
</ul>
<p>2-Hyperthyroidism:</p>
<ul>
<li>Increased production of thyroid hormones.</li>
<li>Graves disease characterized by protruding eyes &amp; extreme nervousness.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="thyroid-hormone-preparations">Thyroid hormone preparations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thyroid-hormone-preparations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Levothyroxine sodium (T4) (synthroid)</li>
<li>Liothyronine sodium (T3) (cytomel)</li>
<li>Liotrix (Mixture of T4+ T3) (Euthroid, thyrolar).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="action-of-thyroid-hormones">Action of thyroid hormones:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#action-of-thyroid-hormones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>178</p>
<p>1- Essential for normal physical &amp; mental development of the fetus &amp; infants.
2- Increase the BMR &amp; blood sugar level, increase synthesis of fatty acids, and decrease plasma cholesterol &amp; triglycerides.
3- Increase H.R. &amp; peripheral resistance.
4- Decrease thyroid releasing hormone (TRH) &amp; TSH from the hypothalamus &amp; anterior pituitary.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indications">Indications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Replacement therapy in primary &amp; secondary myxedema, nontoxic goiter, and chronic thyroiditis.</li>
<li>With aritithyroid drugs for thyrotoxicosis to prevent hypothyroidism.</li>
<li>Surgical removal of thyroid gland.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="contraindications">Contraindications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>C.N.S.: Nervousness, headache, insomnia, tremor.
C.V.S.: Arrhythmias, palpitations, angina pectoris, dyspnea &amp; hypertension.
GIT: Abdominal Cramps., appetite changes, nausea, vomiting, diarrhea &amp; loss of weight.
179
Others: Menstrual irregularities, hyperthyroidism, sweating, allergic reaction, hyperglycemia.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-considerations">Nursing considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1- The treatment is initiated slowly (with small doses) &amp; gradually increased.
2- Store medications in cool dark place.
3- Take complete nursing history.
4- Note if the client is taking antidiabetic drugs &amp; document.
5- Take baseline ECG. then at regular intervals.
6- Monitor thyroid function closely.
7- Observe client for side effects.
8- Monitor PT &amp; PTT closely since the drug increases hypoprothrombinemia.
9- Monitor HR &amp; B.P. closely for cardiac patients.
10- Instruct the client to report side effects e.g. weight loss &amp; nervousness to physician.
11- Have dietitian counsel clients regarding diet according to the energy demands.
12- Female client should record menstrual irregularities.
13- Encourage the client to keep follow-up visits.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="antithyroid-drugs">Antithyroid Drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antithyroid-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Anti-thyroid drugs include thiourcil derivatives &amp; large doses of iodide.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="action">Action:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<p><strong>Oral Contraceptives</strong></p>
<p><strong>Estrogen- Progesterone Combinations</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>The most effective form of birth control available.</li>
</ul>
<p>|  - | There are 3 types of combinations:
1- Monophasic: contain the same amount of estrogen &amp; progesterone in  |
| --- | --- |</p>
<p>each tablet.</p>
<p>2- Biphasic: contain the same amount of estrogen in each tablet but the progestin content is lower for the first 10 days of the cycle &amp; higher in the last 11 days.</p>
<p>181</p>
<p>3- Triphasic: The estrogen content may be the same or may vary throughout the medication cycle. The progestin content varies.</p>
<p><strong>N.B.:</strong> The purpose of biphasic &amp; triphasic products is to give or provide</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>hormones in a manner similar to that occurring physiologically.</p>
<ul>
<li>Other types of oral contraceptives is the progestin-only (mini-pill) product which contain a small amount of progestin in each tablet.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Action:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Inhibit ovulation due to inhibition of L.H. &amp; F.S.H. (by negative feedback mechanism) which are necessary for development of the ova, changes in the endometrium &amp; cervical mucosa so that the penetration of sperm &amp; implantation of ova will not take place.</li>
<li>Promote the regularity of the cycle.</li>
<li>Decrease incidence of dysmenorrhea.</li>
<li>Decrease blood loss during menstruation.</li>
<li>Decrease incidence of endometrial cancer, ectopic pregnancy &amp; pelvic inflammatory diseases.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Uses:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Contraception</li>
<li>Menstrual irregularities</li>
<li>Menopausal symptoms</li>
<li>Endometriosis &amp; hypermenorrhea.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Contraindications:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>History of cerebrovascular diseases.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
